**Expected Answer:** Need to show: (1) holomorphic on upper half-plane H, (2) holomorphic at infinity, (3) G₄((aτ+b)/(cτ+d)) = (cτ+d)⁴ G₄(τ) for (a b; c d) ∈ SL₂(Z). (1) Series converges absolutely and uniformly on compact subsets of H (since exponent 4 > 2), so G₄ is holomorphic. (2) Fourier expansion: G₄(τ) = 2ζ(4) + (2π⁴/45)Σ_{n≥1} σ₃(n)qⁿ where q = e^{2πiτ}. No negative powers of q, so holomorphic at ∞. (3) Transformation: G₄(γτ) = Σ' 1/(mγτ+n)⁴. Write mγτ+n = (m(aτ+b)+n(cτ+d))/(cτ+d) = ((ma+nc)τ+(mb+nd))/(cτ+d). As (m,n) ranges over Z²\{0}, so does (ma+nc, mb+nd) (since γ ∈ SL₂(Z) is invertible over Z). So G₄(γτ) = (cτ+d)⁴ Σ' 1/((ma+nc)τ+(mb+nd))⁴ = (cτ+d)⁴ G₄(τ).
**Skills Tested:** Modular forms, Eisenstein series, transformation laws.

**ID:** AAD-285
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Riemannian Geometry
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Compute the Riemann curvature tensor of the 2-sphere S² with standard metric.
**Expected Answer:** S² with metric ds² = dθ² + sin²θ dφ². Metric tensor: g₁₁ = 1, g₁₂ = 0, g₂₂ = sin²θ. Christoffel symbols: Γ¹₂₂ = -sinθ cosθ, Γ²₁₂ = Γ²₂₁ = cotθ, others zero. Riemann tensor: R^i_{jkl} = ∂_k Γ^i_{lj} - ∂_l Γ^i_{kj} + Γ^i_{km}Γ^m_{lj} - Γ^i_{lm}Γ^m_{kj}. Compute R¹₂₁₂ = ∂₁Γ¹₂₂ - ∂₂Γ¹₁₂ + Γ¹₁ₘΓ^m₂₂ - Γ¹₂ₘΓ^m₁₂ = ∂_θ(-sinθ cosθ) - 0 + 0 - Γ¹₂₂Γ²₁₂ = -cos²θ + sin²θ - (-sinθ cosθ)(cotθ) = -cos²θ + sin²θ + cos²θ = sin²θ. Lower all indices: R₁₂₁₂ = g₁₁ R¹₂₁₂ = sin²θ. Gaussian curvature K = R₁₂₁₂/(g₁₁g₂₂ - g₁₂²) = sin²θ/(1·sin²θ - 0) = 1. So S² has constant curvature 1.
**Skills Tested:** Riemannian geometry, curvature tensors, Christoffel symbols.

**ID:** AAD-286
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Symplectic Geometry
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Prove that the phase space R²ⁿ with standard symplectic form ω = Σ dpᵢ ∧ dqᵢ is a symplectic manifold.
**Expected Answer:** Need to show: (1) ω is closed: dω = 0. (2) ω is non-degenerate: ωⁿ ≠ 0. (1) ω = Σ dpᵢ ∧ dqᵢ. dω = Σ d(dpᵢ ∧ dqᵢ) = Σ (d(dpᵢ) ∧ dqᵢ - dpᵢ ∧ d(dqᵢ)) = 0 since d² = 0. (2) ωⁿ = (Σ dpᵢ ∧ dqᵢ)ⁿ. Expand: only term with all indices distinct survives. ωⁿ = n! dp₁ ∧ dq₁ ∧ ... ∧ dpₙ ∧ dqₙ ≠ 0 (standard volume form). So ω is non-degenerate. Thus (R²ⁿ, ω) is symplectic manifold.
**Skills Tested:** Symplectic geometry, differential forms, non-degeneracy.

**ID:** AAD-287
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Dynamical Systems
**Difficulty Level:** 9
**Question:** Analyze the stability of the fixed point (0,0) for the system x' = -x + y², y' = -y.
**Expected Answer:** Linearization at (0,0): Jacobian J = [[-1, 0], [0, -1]]. Eigenvalues: λ₁ = λ₂ = -1 < 0. Linearized system is stable (both eigenvalues negative). By Hartman-Grobman theorem, nonlinear system is locally topologically conjugate to linearization near hyperbolic fixed point. Since eigenvalues have negative real part and are nonzero (hyperbolic), (0,0) is asymptotically stable for nonlinear system. Alternatively, use Lyapunov function V = x² + y². V' = 2xx' + 2yy' = 2x(-x+y²) + 2y(-y) = -2x² + 2xy² - 2y². Near origin, |2xy²| ≤ 2|x|y² < x² + y² for small x,y. So V' < 0 near origin, confirming asymptotic stability.
**Skills Tested:** Dynamical systems, stability analysis, linearization.

**ID:** AAD-288
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Chaos Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 9
**Question:** Show that the logistic map f(x) = rx(1-x) has a period-2 orbit for r > 3 and find it explicitly.
**Expected Answer:** Period-2 orbit: f(f(x)) = x but f(x) ≠ x. f(x) = rx - rx². f(f(x)) = r(rx-rx²)(1-rx+rx²) = r²x(1-x)(1-rx+rx²). Set f(f(x)) = x: r²x(1-x)(1-rx+rx²) = x. Solutions: x = 0 (fixed point) or r²(1-x)(1-rx+rx²) = 1. Expand: r²(1 - rx + rx² - x + rx² - rx³) = 1. r² - r³x + r³x² - r²x + r³x² - r³x³ = 1. r³x³ - 2r³x² + (r³+r²)x + (1-r²) = 0. We know x = (r-1)/r is fixed point (f(x) = x), so factor out (x - (r-1)/r). After division: r³x² - r²(r+1)x + r(r-1) = 0. Quadratic formula: x = [r²(r+1) ± √(r⁴(r+1)² - 4r⁴(r-1))]/(2r³) = [(r+1) ± √((r+1)² - 4(r-1))]/(2r) = [(r+1) ± √(r²-2r+5)]/(2r). For r > 3, discriminant r²-2r+5 > 0, so two real solutions. These form period-2 orbit {x₁, x₂} where x₁ = [(r+1) + √(r²-2r+5)]/(2r), x₂ = [(r+1) - √(r²-2r+5)]/(2r).
**Skills Tested:** Dynamical systems, bifurcation theory, discrete dynamics.

**ID:** AAD-289
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Fractal Geometry
**Difficulty Level:** 9
**Question:** Compute the Hausdorff dimension of the Cantor set.
**Expected Answer:** Cantor set C constructed by removing middle thirds. At stage n, have 2ⁿ intervals of length 3⁻ⁿ. Hausdorff dimension: dim_H(C) = lim_{n→∞} log(N(ε))/log(1/ε) where N(ε) is number of sets of diameter ε needed to cover C. Take ε = 3⁻ⁿ. Need 2ⁿ intervals to cover. dim_H = lim log(2ⁿ)/log(3ⁿ) = lim n log 2 / (n log 3) = log 2 / log 3 ≈ 0.631. Rigorous proof: show dim_H ≤ log 2/log 3 by covering with 2ⁿ intervals of length 3⁻ⁿ, compute s-dimensional Hausdorff measure. For s = log 2/log 3: H^s(C) ≤ lim 2ⁿ · (3⁻ⁿ)^s = lim 2ⁿ · 3^{-ns} = lim 2ⁿ · 2⁻ⁿ = 1 < ∞. So dim_H ≤ s. Similarly dim_H ≥ s by mass distribution principle.
**Skills Tested:** Fractal geometry, Hausdorff dimension, Cantor set.

**ID:** AAD-290
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Geometric Measure Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** State and prove the isoperimetric inequality in R²: among all closed curves of length L, the circle encloses maximum area A ≤ L²/(4π).
**Expected Answer:** Isoperimetric inequality: L² ≥ 4πA with equality iff curve is circle. Proof sketch (Steiner symmetrization): Given region Ω with boundary ∂Ω of length L and area A. Symmetrize: for each horizontal line, replace intersection with interval of same length centered on y-axis. This preserves area, doesn't increase perimeter. Repeat for vertical direction. Sequence of symmetrizations converges to disk with same area but perimeter ≤ L. For disk: L = 2πr, A = πr², so L² = 4π²r² = 4πA. Since symmetrization doesn't increase L, original L² ≥ 4πA. Equality requires original already a circle. Alternative proof using Fourier analysis or calculus of variations.
**Skills Tested:** Geometric measure theory, isoperimetric inequality, symmetrization.

**ID:** AAD-291
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Geometric Group Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Prove that the free group F₂ on 2 generators is not amenable.
**Expected Answer:** A group G is amenable if has finitely additive left-invariant probability measure on all subsets. F₂ = ⟨a, b⟩. Suppose F₂ amenable. Let μ be invariant measure. Partition F₂ into 4 sets based on first letter of reduced word: S(a) = words starting with a, S(a⁻¹), S(b), S(b⁻¹), plus {e}. Note F₂ = S(a) ∪ aS(a⁻¹) ∪ S(b) ∪ bS(b⁻¹) ∪ {e}. By invariance: μ(S(a)) = μ(aS(a⁻¹)), etc. Also S(a) ∪ S(a⁻¹) ∪ S(b) ∪ S(b⁻¹) ∪ {e} = F₂. Since μ({e}) = 0 (singletons have measure 0 in infinite amenable group), μ(S(a)) + μ(S(a⁻¹)) + μ(S(b)) + μ(S(b⁻¹)) = 1. But S(a) and aS(a⁻¹) are disjoint and their union is F₂ \ S(a⁻¹). So μ(S(a)) + μ(aS(a⁻¹)) = 1 - μ(S(a⁻¹)). By invariance, 2μ(S(a)) = 1 - μ(S(a⁻¹)). Similarly 2μ(S(b)) = 1 - μ(S(b⁻¹)). Sum: 2[μ(S(a))+μ(S(b))] = 2 - [μ(S(a⁻¹))+μ(S(b⁻¹))] = 2 - [1 - μ(S(a)) - μ(S(b))]. So 2[μ(S(a))+μ(S(b))] = 1 + μ(S(a)) + μ(S(b)), giving μ(S(a)) + μ(S(b)) = 1. Similarly μ(S(a⁻¹)) + μ(S(b⁻¹)) = 1. But total is 1, contradiction.
**Skills Tested:** Geometric group theory, amenability, paradoxical decompositions.

**ID:** AAD-292
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Operator Algebras
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Prove that every C*-algebra is isometrically *-isomorphic to a closed *-subalgebra of B(H) for some Hilbert space H (Gelfand-Naimark theorem).
**Expected Answer:** Gelfand-Naimark-Segal (GNS) construction: given state φ on C*-algebra A, construct representation. Define sesquilinear form ⟨a, b⟩ = φ(b*a). Quotient by null space N = {a : φ(a*a) = 0}. Complete to get Hilbert space H_φ. Define π_φ(a)[b] = [ab]. Check well-defined, bounded, *-homomorphism. Take direct sum over all states: H = ⊕_φ H_φ, π = ⊕_φ π_φ. Then π is faithful (injective) *-homomorphism from A to B(H). By C*-identity, ||π(a)|| = ||a||, so isometric. Image is closed *-subalgebra. Thus A embeds into B(H).
**Skills Tested:** Operator algebras, C*-algebras, GNS construction.

**ID:** AAD-293
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** K-Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Compute K⁰(S²) (topological K-theory of 2-sphere).
**Expected Answer:** K⁰(X) = Grothendieck group of vector bundles over X. For S²: use clutching construction. S² = D⁺ ∪ D⁻ (upper/lower hemispheres) glued along equator S¹. Vector bundles over S² classified by clutching functions f: S¹ → GLₙ(C) up to homotopy. π₁(GLₙ(C)) = π₁(U(n)) = Z for n ≥ 1. So bundles classified by integer (first Chern number). K⁰(S²) = Z ⊕ Z where first Z is rank, second is Chern number. Explicitly: trivial bundle has (rank, c₁) = (1, 0). Tautological bundle over CP¹ ≅ S² has (1, -1). So K⁰(S²) ≅ Z[H]/(H-1)² where H is tautological bundle, using relation (H-1)² = 0.
**Skills Tested:** K-theory, vector bundles, clutching construction.

**ID:** AAD-294
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Cohomology Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Compute the de Rham cohomology H*(T²) of the torus.
**Expected Answer:** T² = S¹ × S¹. Use Künneth formula: H^k(X × Y) = ⊕_{i+j=k} H^i(X) ⊗ H^j(Y). H*(S¹) = H⁰ ⊕ H¹ = R ⊕ R (generated by 1 and dθ). So H⁰(T²) = H⁰(S¹) ⊗ H⁰(S¹) = R (generated by 1). H¹(T²) = H⁰ ⊗ H¹ ⊕ H¹ ⊗ H⁰ = R ⊕ R (generated by dθ₁ and dθ₂). H²(T²) = H¹ ⊗ H¹ = R (generated by dθ₁ ∧ dθ₂). H^k = 0 for k > 2. So H*(T²) = R in degrees 0, 2 and R² in degree 1. Betti numbers: b₀ = 1, b₁ = 2, b₂ = 1. Euler characteristic: χ = 1 - 2 + 1 = 0.
**Skills Tested:** de Rham cohomology, Künneth formula, torus.

**ID:** AAD-295
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Characteristic Classes
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Prove that the first Chern class c₁(E) of a complex line bundle E over X classifies line bundles: there is a bijection between isomorphism classes of line bundles and H²(X; Z).
**Expected Answer:** Line bundles classified by transition functions g_{αβ}: U_α ∩ U_β → C* = U(1). These satisfy cocycle condition. Čech cohomology H¹(X, U(1)) classifies bundles. From exponential sequence 0 → Z → R → U(1) → 0 (where R → U(1) is t ↦ e^{2πit}), get long exact sequence: ... → H¹(X, R) → H¹(X, U(1)) → H²(X, Z) → H²(X, R) → ... Since R is fine sheaf (partition of unity), H^k(X, R) = 0 for k > 0 (de Rham theorem). So H¹(X, U(1)) ≅ H²(X, Z). First Chern class c₁: LineBundles(X) → H²(X; Z) is this isomorphism. Explicitly: c₁(E) = [ω/2π] where ω is curvature of connection on E.
**Skills Tested:** Characteristic classes, Chern classes, classification of bundles.

**ID:** AAD-296
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Morse Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** State and prove the Morse inequalities relating critical points of a Morse function to Betti numbers.
**Expected Answer:** Morse function f: M → R has non-degenerate critical points. Let cₖ = number of critical points of index k. Morse inequalities: (weak) cₖ ≥ bₖ (Betti numbers). (strong) Σ(-1)^k cₖ t^k = Σ bₖ t^k + (1+t)Q(t) for some polynomial Q with non-negative coefficients. Proof sketch: Build M by attaching handles at critical points. Index k critical point adds k-handle (D^k × D^{n-k}). Cellular chain complex: Cₖ = Z^{cₖ}. Homology Hₖ = ker ∂ₖ / im ∂ₖ₊₁. So bₖ = rank Hₖ ≤ rank Cₖ = cₖ. For strong form: Euler characteristic χ = Σ(-1)^k cₖ = Σ(-1)^k bₖ. Poincaré polynomial P(t) = Σ bₖ t^k, Morse polynomial M(t) = Σ cₖ t^k. Then M(t) - P(t) = (1+t)Q(t) since both have same value at t = -1 (Euler char) and coefficients of M - P must be non-negative (since cₖ ≥ bₖ).
**Skills Tested:** Morse theory, critical points, topology.

**ID:** AAD-297
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Index Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** State the Atiyah-Singer index theorem for elliptic operators.
**Expected Answer:** Let D: Γ(E) → Γ(F) be elliptic differential operator on compact manifold M. Index: ind(D) = dim ker D - dim coker D. Atiyah-Singer index theorem: ind(D) = ∫_M ch(σ(D)) · td(TM ⊗ C) where σ(D) is symbol of D (element of K-theory of T*M), ch is Chern character, td is Todd class of complexified tangent bundle. For Dirac operator on spin manifold: ind(D) = Â(M) (A-hat genus). For signature operator: ind = signature(M) = L(M) (L-genus). For Dolbeault operator on complex manifold: ind = χ(O_M) = ∫ ch(O) · td(TM) (holomorphic Euler characteristic). Theorem connects analysis (index) to topology (characteristic classes).
**Skills Tested:** Index theory, elliptic operators, characteristic classes.

**ID:** AAD-298
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Spectral Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Prove the spectral theorem for compact self-adjoint operators on Hilbert space.
**Expected Answer:** Let T: H → H be compact and self-adjoint (T = T*). Need to show H has orthonormal basis of eigenvectors. Step 1: ||T|| = sup{|⟨Tx, x⟩| : ||x|| = 1} (since T self-adjoint). Step 2: If T ≠ 0, ∃ eigenvalue λ with |λ| = ||T||. Let λₙ be sequence with |⟨Txₙ, xₙ⟩| → ||T||. Since T compact, Txₙ has convergent subsequence Tx_{nₖ} → y. Show y = λx for some unit x, and Tx = λx. Step 3: Let H₁ = ker(T - λI). H₁ is closed, T-invariant. Let H₂ = H₁^⊥. T maps H₂ to H₂ (since T self-adjoint). Restrict T to H₂, repeat. Get sequence of eigenvalues λ₁, λ₂, ... with eigenvectors e₁, e₂, .... Since T compact, λₙ → 0. Span{eₙ} is dense: if x ⊥ all eₙ, then x ∈ ∩Hₙ, but ||T|_{Hₙ}|| = |λₙ| → 0, so T = 0 on ∩Hₙ, meaning x ∈ ker T, but then Tx = 0 = 0·x, so x is eigenvector with eigenvalue 0, already included. Thus {eₙ} is orthonormal basis.
**Skills Tested:** Spectral theory, compact operators, Hilbert spaces.

**ID:** AAD-299
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Scattering Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the Lippmann-Schwinger equation in quantum scattering theory.
**Expected Answer:** Scattering: particle with Hamiltonian H = H₀ + V where H₀ = -ℏ²∇²/2m (free), V is potential (short-range). Want solutions ψ of Hψ = Eψ that look like plane waves plus outgoing spherical waves at infinity. Lippmann-Schwinger equation: |ψ⁽⁺⁾⟩ = |φ⟩ + G₀⁺(E) V |ψ⁽⁺⁾⟩ where |φ⟩ is free state (H₀|φ⟩ = E|φ⟩), G₀⁺(E) = lim_{ε→0⁺} (E - H₀ + iε)⁻¹ is retarded Green's function. In position space: ψ⁽⁺⁾(r) = φ(r) + ∫ G₀⁺(r, r'; E) V(r') ψ⁽⁺⁾(r') d³r'. Green's function: G₀⁺(r, r'; E) = -m/(2πℏ²) e^{ik|r-r'|}/|r-r'| where k = √(2mE)/ℏ. Asymptotically: ψ⁽⁺⁾(r) → e^{ik·r} + f(θ, φ) e^{ikr}/r where f is scattering amplitude. Cross section: dσ/dΩ = |f|². Lippmann-Schwinger is integral equation for ψ, solved iteratively (Born series).
**Skills Tested:** Quantum mechanics, scattering theory, integral equations.

**ID:** AAD-300
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Quantum Field Theory — Path Integrals
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Derive the path integral formulation of quantum mechanics from the Schrödinger equation.
**Expected Answer:** Start with ⟨x_f|e^{-iHt/ℏ}|x_i⟩. Divide time: t = Nε. Insert complete sets: ⟨x_f|e^{-iHt/ℏ}|x_i⟩ = ∫...∫ ⟨x_f|e^{-iHε/ℏ}|x_{N-1}⟩...⟨x₁|e^{-iHε/ℏ}|x_i⟩ dx₁...dx_{N-1}. For small ε: H = p²/2m + V(x). ⟨x_{j+1}|e^{-iHε/ℏ}|x_j⟩ ≈ ⟨x_{j+1}|e^{-ip²ε/2mℏ}e^{-iVε/ℏ}|x_j⟩ = e^{-iV(x_j)ε/ℏ} ⟨x_{j+1}|e^{-ip²ε/2mℏ}|x_j⟩. Momentum space: ⟨x|p⟩ = e^{ipx/ℏ}/√(2πℏ). So ⟨x_{j+1}|e^{-ip²ε/2mℏ}|x_j⟩ = ∫ dp/(2πℏ) e^{ip(x_{j+1}-x_j)/ℏ} e^{-ip²ε/2mℏ}. Gaussian integral: = √(m/2πiℏε) exp[im(x_{j+1}-x_j)²/2ℏε]. Product: ⟨x_f|e^{-iHt/ℏ}|x_i⟩ = lim_{N→∞} (m/2πiℏε)^{N/2} ∫...∫ exp[i/ℏ Σⱼ (m(x_{j+1}-x_j)²/2ε - V(x_j)ε)] dx₁...dx_{N-1}. As ε → 0, sum → ∫₀ᵗ L(x, ẋ) dt' where L = mẋ²/2 - V is Lagrangian. So ⟨x_f|e^{-iHt/ℏ}|x_i⟩ = ∫ Dx exp[iS[x]/ℏ] where S = ∫ L dt is action, and ∫ Dx is formal path integral measure.
**Skills Tested:** Quantum field theory, path integrals, quantum mechanics.

**ID:** AAD-301
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Gauge Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the Yang-Mills action and derive the Yang-Mills equations.
**Expected Answer:** Gauge field: connection A on principal G-bundle over spacetime M. Curvature: F = dA + A ∧ A (field strength). Yang-Mills action: S = -1/2 ∫_M tr(F ∧ *F) where * is Hodge star. In components: S = -1/4 ∫ tr(F_{μν} F^{μν}) d⁴x. Vary: δS = -∫ tr(δA ∧ d*F + δA ∧ [A, *F]) = -∫ tr(δA ∧ (d*F + [A, *F])) = -∫ tr(δA ∧ D*F) where D is covariant derivative. Set δS = 0 for all δA: D*F = 0 (Yang-Mills equations). In components: D_μ F^{μν} = 0 where D_μ = ∂_μ + [A_μ, ·]. These are non-linear PDEs for A. Bianchi identity: DF = 0 (analogous to dF = 0 in electromagnetism). Yang-Mills equations generalize Maxwell's equations to non-abelian gauge groups.
**Skills Tested:** Gauge theory, Yang-Mills, differential geometry.

**ID:** AAD-302
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** General Relativity — Einstein Equations
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Derive the Einstein field equations from the Einstein-Hilbert action.
**Expected Answer:** Einstein-Hilbert action: S = ∫ (R/2κ + L_matter) √(-g) d⁴x where R is Ricci scalar, κ = 8πG/c⁴. Vary with respect to metric g^{μν}: δS = ∫ [δ(R√-g)/2κ + δ(L_matter √-g)] d⁴x. δ√-g = -1/2 √-g g_{μν} δg^{μν}. δR = R_{μν} δg^{μν} + ∇_σ v^σ (boundary term). So δ(R√-g) = √-g (R_{μν} - 1/2 R g_{μν}) δg^{μν} + boundary. δ(L_matter √-g) = -1/2 √-g T_{μν} δg^{μν} where T_{μν} = -2/√-g δ(L_matter √-g)/δg^{μν} is stress-energy tensor. Setting δS = 0: R_{μν} - 1/2 R g_{μν} = κ T_{μν}. These are Einstein field equations: G_{μν} = κ T_{μν} where G_{μν} = R_{μν} - 1/2 R g_{μν} is Einstein tensor.
**Skills Tested:** General relativity, variational principle, Einstein equations.

**ID:** AAD-303
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** String Theory — Worldsheet
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Derive the equations of motion for the bosonic string from the Polyakov action.
**Expected Answer:** Polyakov action: S = -T/2 ∫ d²σ √-h h^{ab} ∂_a X^μ ∂_b X^ν η_{μν} where T is string tension, h_{ab} is worldsheet metric, X^μ(σ) are embedding coordinates. Vary X^μ: δS = -T ∫ d²σ √-h h^{ab} ∂_a X_μ ∂_b δX^μ = T ∫ d²σ ∂_a(√-h h^{ab} ∂_b X_μ) δX^μ (integration by parts, assuming δX vanishes on boundary). Set δS = 0: ∂_a(√-h h^{ab} ∂_b X^μ) = 0. In conformal gauge h_{ab} = e^φ η_{ab}: □X^μ = η^{ab} ∂_a ∂_b X^μ = 0 (wave equation on worldsheet). Vary h^{ab}: get stress-energy tensor T_{ab} = ∂_a X · ∂_b X - 1/2 h_{ab} h^{cd} ∂_c X · ∂_d X = 0 (constraint equations). In conformal gauge: T_{zz} = ∂_+ X · ∂_+ X = 0, T_{z̄z̄} = ∂_- X · ∂_- X = 0 (Virasoro constraints).
**Skills Tested:** String theory, variational principle, conformal field theory.

**ID:** AAD-304
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Conformal Field Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the operator product expansion (OPE) in 2D conformal field theory.
**Expected Answer:** OPE: product of two local operators at nearby points can be expanded as sum of local operators at one point: A(z, z̄) B(w, w̄) = Σ_k C_k(z-w, z̄-w̄) O_k(w, w̄). In holomorphic CFT: A(z) B(w) = Σ_k C_k(z-w) O_k(w). Coefficients C_k(z-w) are determined by conformal symmetry. For primary fields: φ_i(z) φ_j(w) = Σ_k c_{ijk} (z-w)^{h_k-h_i-h_j} φ_k(w) + descendants. Example: free boson ∂X(z) ∂X(w) = -1/(2(z-w)²) + :∂X ∂X:(w) + .... OPE encodes algebra of operators. Associativity of OPE (crossing symmetry) constrains CFT. OPE coefficients c_{ijk} and conformal dimensions h_i determine correlation functions via conformal bootstrap.
**Skills Tested:** Conformal field theory, operator product expansion, 2D CFT.

**ID:** AAD-305
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Vertex Algebras
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Define a vertex algebra and explain its relation to conformal field theory.
**Expected Answer:** Vertex algebra: vector space V with state-operator correspondence: each v ∈ V maps to vertex operator Y(v, z) = Σ_{n∈Z} v_n z^{-n-1} where v_n ∈ End(V). Axioms: (1) Vacuum: Y(|0⟩, z) = id, Y(v, z)|0⟩|_{z=0} = v. (2) Translation: [L_{-1}, Y(v, z)] = ∂_z Y(v, z) where L_{-1} is translation operator. (3) Locality: (z-w)^N [Y(u, z), Y(v, w)] = 0 for N >> 0 (operators commute up to poles). Relation to CFT: vertex algebra encodes chiral (holomorphic) sector of 2D CFT. States correspond to fields via state-field correspondence. OPE encoded in locality axiom. Virasoro algebra action gives conformal symmetry. Examples: free boson, free fermion, affine Lie algebras, W-algebras, Moonshine module V^♮.
**Skills Tested:** Vertex algebras, conformal field theory, mathematical physics.

**ID:** AAD-306
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Mirror Symmetry
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the basic idea of mirror symmetry for Calabi-Yau manifolds.
**Expected Answer:** Mirror symmetry: conjecture (now theorem in many cases) that for Calabi-Yau manifold X, exists mirror Calabi-Yau Y such that complex geometry of X equals symplectic geometry of Y and vice versa. Specifically: Hodge numbers swap: h^{1,1}(X) = h^{1,2}(Y), h^{2,1}(X) = h^{1,1}(Y). A-model (symplectic, Gromov-Witten invariants counting holomorphic curves) on X equals B-model (complex, variations of Hodge structure) on Y. Physical origin: type IIA string on X × R^{3,1} equivalent to type IIB on Y × R^{3,1}. Mathematical consequences: compute Gromov-Witten invariants of X via period integrals on Y (much easier). Example: quintic threefold X ⊂ P⁴ has mirror Y constructed as resolution of quotient of Fermat quintic. Number of rational curves of degree d on X computed from mirror map.
**Skills Tested:** Mirror symmetry, Calabi-Yau manifolds, string theory.

**ID:** AAD-307
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Topological Quantum Field Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Define a topological quantum field theory (TQFT) in the sense of Atiyah.
**Expected Answer:** TQFT (d-dimensional): symmetric monoidal functor Z from Cob_d (category of (d-1)-manifolds and d-dimensional cobordisms) to Vect (category of vector spaces). Assigns: to closed (d-1)-manifold Σ: vector space Z(Σ) (state space). To cobordism M: ∂M = Σ_{in}^* ⊔ Σ_{out}: linear map Z(M): Z(Σ_{in}) → Z(Σ_{out}). Functorial: Z(M₁ ∪_{Σ} M₂) = Z(M₂) ∘ Z(M₁). Monoidal: Z(Σ₁ ⊔ Σ₂) = Z(Σ₁) ⊗ Z(Σ₂). Examples: Chern-Simons theory (d=3), BF theory, Dijkgraaf-Witten theory (finite gauge group). Properties: Z(Σ) finite-dimensional, Z(M) depends only on topology of M (metric-independent). Partition function Z(M) for closed d-manifold is invariant. TQFTs classify topological invariants and relate to quantum groups, knot invariants.
**Skills Tested:** Topological quantum field theory, category theory, mathematical physics.

**ID:** AAD-308
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Knot Theory — Jones Polynomial
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Define the Jones polynomial and compute it for the trefoil knot.
**Expected Answer:** Jones polynomial V(K) ∈ Z[t^{±1/2}] defined via skein relation: t⁻¹ V(L₊) - t V(L₋) = (t^{1/2} - t^{-1/2}) V(L₀) where L₊, L₋, L₀ differ at one crossing (positive, negative, smoothed). Normalization: V(unknot) = 1. Trefoil (right-handed): 3 crossings, all positive. Resolve one crossing: L₊ = trefoil, L₋ = unknot (after simplification), L₀ = Hopf link. Apply skein relation recursively. Result: V(trefoil) = -t⁻⁴ + t⁻³ + t⁻¹. Check: V(trefoil)|_{t=1} = -1 + 1 + 1 = 1 (since V(1) = 1 for any knot). Jones polynomial distinguishes trefoil from its mirror (left-handed trefoil has V = -t⁴ + t³ + t, different). Origin: from representation theory of quantum group U_q(sl₂) or from statistical mechanics (Potts model).
**Skills Tested:** Knot theory, Jones polynomial, skein relations.

**ID:** AAD-309
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Floer Homology
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the basic idea of Floer homology for Lagrangian intersections.
**Expected Answer:** Floer homology: infinite-dimensional Morse theory. Given Lagrangians L₀, L₁ in symplectic manifold (M, ω), intersecting transversely. Generators of chain complex: intersection points L₀ ∩ L₁. Differential: count pseudo-holomorphic strips u: R × [0,1] → M with u(s, 0) ∈ L₀, u(s, 1) ∈ L₁, ∂_s u + J ∂_t u = 0 (Cauchy-Riemann), u(-∞) = x, u(+∞) = y for intersection points x, y. Differential ∂x = Σ_y n(x, y) y where n(x, y) is (signed) count of such strips (modulo translation). ∂² = 0 (by analyzing 1-parameter families, boundary of moduli space consists of broken strips). Floer homology HF(L₀, L₁) = ker ∂ / im ∂. Arnold conjecture: HF(L, L) ≅ H*(L) (if L is Hamiltonian perturbation of itself). Floer homology is symplectic invariant, relates to quantum cohomology, mirror symmetry.
**Skills Tested:** Floer homology, symplectic geometry, pseudo-holomorphic curves.

**ID:** AAD-310
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Derived Categories
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Define the derived category D(Ab) of abelian groups and explain its universal property.
**Expected Answer:** Start with category Ch(Ab) of chain complexes of abelian groups. Quasi-isomorphism: chain map f: A → B inducing isomorphism on homology. Derived category D(Ab): localize Ch(Ab) at quasi-isomorphisms. Objects: chain complexes. Morphisms: roofs A ← C → B where left arrow is quasi-isomorphism (formally invert quasi-isos). Universal property: D(Ab) is initial among categories with functor from Ch(Ab) sending quasi-isos to isomorphisms. Equivalently: D(Ab) ≅ K(Ab)[Q⁻¹] where K(Ab) is homotopy category, Q is quasi-isomorphisms. Derived functors: left derived LF of right exact F: compute by replacing with projective resolution. Right derived RF of left exact G: injective resolution. Example: Ext^n(A, B) = H^n(R Hom(A, B)) in D(Ab). Derived category provides natural setting for derived functors and duality theories.
**Skills Tested:** Derived categories, homological algebra, triangulated categories.

**ID:** AAD-311
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Motivic Cohomology
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the basic idea of motivic cohomology for algebraic varieties.
**Expected Answer:** Motivic cohomology: universal cohomology theory for algebraic varieties, analogous to singular cohomology for topology. For smooth variety X over field k: H^{p,q}(X, Z) (bigraded). Properties: (1) H^{2q,q}(X, Z) = CH^q(X) (Chow groups). (2) H^{p,q}(X, Z) = 0 for p > 2q or p < q. (3) Relates to K-theory: K_n(X) ⊗ Q = ⊕_{q} H^{2q-n, q}(X, Q). Construction: via motivic complexes Z(q) in derived category (Bloch, Voevodsky). Z(q) = complex of sheaves with transfers. Motivic cohomology satisfies: Nisnevich descent, A¹-homotopy invariance, transfer maps. Beilinson conjectures: relate motivic cohomology to special values of L-functions. Voevodsky proved Milnor conjecture (and Bloch-Kato) using motivic cohomology and motivic Steenrod algebra.
**Skills Tested:** Motivic cohomology, algebraic geometry, algebraic K-theory.

**ID:** AAD-312
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Perfectoid Spaces
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Define a perfectoid space and explain its significance in p-adic geometry.
**Expected Answer:** Perfectoid field: complete non-archimedean field K with non-discrete valuation of characteristic p > 0, or mixed characteristic (0, p) with surjective Frobenius on O_K/p. Example: Q_p(p^{1/p^∞})^ (completion of Q_p(All p-power roots of p)). Perfectoid space: adic space X over perfectoid field that is locally (in pro-étale topology) isomorphic to Spa(K⟨T^{1/p^∞}⟩). Key property: tilting equivalence. For perfectoid K of mixed characteristic, K^♭ = inverse limit of K under Frobenius (perfectoid of char p). Tilting: category of perfectoid spaces over K equivalent to category over K^♭. Significance: (1) Proves weight-monodromy conjecture in some cases. (2) Scholze's proof of local Langlands for GL_n over p-adic fields. (3) Relates p-adic Hodge theory in mixed and equal characteristic. (4) New approach to p-adic geometry, analogous to passage from characteristic 0 to char p.
**Skills Tested:** p-adic geometry, perfectoid spaces, arithmetic geometry.

**ID:** AAD-313
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Langlands Program
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** State the local Langlands correspondence for GL_n over a p-adic field.
**Expected Answer:** Local Langlands for GL_n over p-adic field F: bijection between (1) irreducible smooth representations π of GL_n(F) and (2) n-dimensional Frobenius-semisimple Weil-Deligne representations φ of Weil group W_F. Properties: (1) Preserves L-functions and ε-factors: L(s, π) = L(s, φ), ε(s, π, ψ) = ε(s, φ, ψ). (2) Compatible with twists: π ⊗ χ ↔ φ ⊗ χ. (3) For n=1: class field theory, π ↔ χ (characters of F* ↔ characters of W_F^{ab}). (4) Supercuspidal π ↔ irreducible φ. (5) Functoriality: maps between groups induce maps on representations matching Galois side. Proved: n=1 (class field theory), n=2 (Kutzko, for F = Q_p), general n (Harris-Taylor, Henniart, using global methods and trace formula). Deep connection between representation theory and arithmetic.
**Skills Tested:** Langlands program, representation theory, number theory.

**ID:** AAD-314
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Geometric Langlands
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the geometric Langlands correspondence.
**Expected Answer:** Geometric Langlands: categorical version of Langlands over complex curves. For complex curve X, reductive group G, Langlands dual group Ĝ: equivalence of categories D-mod(Bun_G(X)) ≅ QCoh(LocSys_{Ĝ}(X)). Left side: D-modules on moduli stack of G-bundles on X (automorphic side). Right side: quasi-coherent sheaves on moduli stack of Ĝ-local systems on X (Galois side). For G = GL₁: D-mod(Bun_{GL₁}) = D-mod(Pic(X)) ↔ QCoh(LocSys_{GL₁}) = QCoh(Pic^♭(X)) (Fourier-Mukai transform). For general G: much deeper, involves factorization algebras, chiral algebras, quantum groups. Connections: (1) 4D N=4 supersymmetric gauge theory (Kapustin-Witten). (2) Quantization of Hitchin system. (3) Categorification of classical Langlands. Active research area with deep connections to mathematical physics.
**Skills Tested:** Geometric Langlands, algebraic geometry, representation theory.

**ID:** AAD-315
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Inter-universal Teichmüller Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Summarize Mochizuki's approach to proving the abc conjecture using inter-universal Teichmüller theory.
**Expected Answer:** abc conjecture: for ε > 0, only finitely many coprime triples (a, b, c) with a + b = c and c > rad(abc)^{1+ε} where rad is product of distinct prime factors. Mochizuki's approach (IUT): (1) Start with number field F and elliptic curve E/F. (2) Construct "Hodge-Arakelov theory" relating arithmetic and geometry. (3) Introduce "Frobenioid theory" — categorical framework generalizing Frobenius maps in char p to mixed characteristic. (4) "Inter-universal" aspect: work with multiple "universes" (copies of number field) related by "theta-links" and "Frobenius-like maps". (5) Compare "label structures" across universes to bound heights. Claim: IUT gives inequality implying abc. Status: controversial. Mochizuki and collaborators claim proof complete. Many experts (Scholze, Stix) identified gaps in proof of "Inequality III". Debate ongoing. If correct, would be revolutionary new approach to Diophantine geometry.
**Skills Tested:** Arithmetic geometry, abc conjecture, inter-universal Teichmüller theory.

**ID:** AAD-316
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Anabelian Geometry
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain Grothendieck's anabelian geometry conjecture.
**Expected Answer:** Anabelian geometry: certain algebraic varieties are determined by their étale fundamental group. Conjecture (Grothendieck 1983): Let X, Y be smooth proper curves of genus g ≥ 2 over number field k. If π₁^{et}(X) ≅ π₁^{et}(Y) (as outer Galois representations), then X ≅ Y over k. More precisely: Hom_k(X, Y) ≅ Hom_{G_k}(π₁^{et}(Y), π₁^{et}(X)) (outer). Status: proved for genus g ≥ 2 over number fields by Mochizuki (1999) using p-adic Teichmüller theory. For affine curves: Tamagawa (1997), Mochizuki. Higher dimensions: open, active research. Philosophical meaning: arithmetic geometry of variety encoded in fundamental group (analogous to how topology of manifold determined by π₁ in some cases). Connects to Grothendieck's "esquisse d'un programme" — understanding absolute Galois group G_Q through its action on geometric fundamental groups.
**Skills Tested:** Anabelian geometry, étale fundamental group, arithmetic geometry.

**ID:** AAD-317
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Hodge Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** State the Hodge decomposition theorem for compact Kähler manifolds.
**Expected Answer:** Let X be compact Kähler manifold of complex dimension n. Hodge decomposition: H^k(X, C) = ⊕_{p+q=k} H^{p,q}(X) where H^{p,q} = H^q(X, Ω^p) (Dolbeault cohomology). Properties: (1) H^{p,q} = H^{q,p} (complex conjugation). (2) dim H^{p,q} = h^{p,q} (Hodge numbers). (3) Hodge symmetry: h^{p,q} = h^{n-p, n-q} (Serre duality). (4) Hard Lefschetz: cup product with [ω]^{n-k}: H^k → H^{2n-k} is isomorphism for k ≤ n. (5) Hodge-Riemann bilinear relations: primitive cohomology has definite Hermitian form. Consequences: (1) Betti numbers b_k = Σ_{p+q=k} h^{p,q} are even for k odd. (2) Hodge numbers constrain topology. (3) Hodge structure on cohomology (polarized Hodge structure). Proof: Δ_d = 2Δ_∂ = 2Δ_∂̄ (Laplacians). Harmonic forms: H^k ≅ H^k_{dR} ≅ ⊕ H^{p,q}. Uses Kähler identities [Λ, ∂] = -i∂̄* etc.
**Skills Tested:** Hodge theory, Kähler geometry, algebraic geometry.

**ID:** AAD-318
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** p-adic Hodge Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the basic comparison theorem in p-adic Hodge theory relating étale and de Rham cohomology.
**Expected Answer:** For proper smooth variety X over p-adic field K: comparison isomorphisms relate different cohomology theories. (1) Fontaine-Messing, Faltings, Tsuji: H^k_{et}(X_{K̄}, Q_p) ⊗ B_{dR} ≅ H^k_{dR}(X/K) ⊗ B_{dR} (de Rham comparison). (2) B_{cris} comparison: H^k_{et} ⊗ B_{cris} ≅ H^k_{cris}(X/W) ⊗ B_{cris} (crystalline comparison, for X good reduction). (3) B_{HT} comparison: H^k_{et} ⊗ B_{HT} ≅ ⊕_q H^{k-q}(X, Ω^q) ⊗ B_{HT}(q) (Hodge-Tate comparison). Here B_{dR}, B_{cris}, B_{HT} are Fontaine's period rings (certain p-adic Banach algebras with extra structure). Consequence: p-adic Galois representations from geometry are "de Rham" (or crystalline, Hodge-Tate). Fontaine's functor D_{dR}: Rep_{p-adic}(G_K) → Fil-K-vect. Geometric representations land in admissible ones. Deep connection between p-adic Galois representations and linear algebra data (filtered φ-modules).
**Skills Tested:** p-adic Hodge theory, comparison theorems, arithmetic geometry.

**ID:** AAD-319
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Motivic Homotopy Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the basic framework of motivic homotopy theory.
**Expected Answer:** Motivic homotopy theory: homotopy theory for algebraic varieties, analogous to classical homotopy theory for spaces. Constructed by Morel-Voevodsky (1999). Start with category Sm/k of smooth schemes over field k. Localize with respect to: (1) A¹-homotopy: X × A¹ → X is weak equivalence. (2) Nisnevich topology: Nisnevich covers become equivalences. Result: motivic homotopy category H(k). Objects: simplicial presheaves on Sm/k. Weak equivalences: A¹-local, Nisnevich-local equivalences. Key features: (1) P¹ = S¹ ∧ G_m (sphere is product of topological circle and algebraic circle). (2) Bigraded cohomology theories: H^{p,q} (p = topological, q = algebraic). (3) Motivic spheres: S^{p,q} = (S¹)^{∧(p-q)} ∧ (G_m)^{∧q}. (4) Motivic stable homotopy category SH(k): invert P¹. Applications: (1) Define motivic cohomology, K-theory. (2) Prove Milnor conjecture (Voevodsky). (3) Compute motivic homotopy groups of spheres (related to classical via realization functors).
**Skills Tested:** Motivic homotopy theory, algebraic geometry, homotopy theory.

**ID:** AAD-320
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Derived Algebraic Geometry
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the basic idea of derived algebraic geometry.
**Expected Answer:** Derived algebraic geometry: enhancement of classical algebraic geometry where spaces have "derived" or "homotopical" structure. Classical: schemes built from commutative rings. Derived: built from simplicial commutative rings or E_∞-ring spectra (commutative ring spectra). Motivation: (1) Better intersection theory: derived fiber product X ×^L_Z Y correctly computes Tor. (2) Deformation theory: derived structure encodes obstruction theory. (3) Moduli problems: derived moduli spaces have correct tangent complexes. Construction: affine derived scheme Spec A where A is simplicial commutative ring. Derived stack: sheaf of spaces on affine derived schemes. Key examples: (1) Derived moduli of perfect complexes. (2) Derived mapping stacks. (3) Shifted symplectic structures (Pantev-Toën-Vaquié-Vezzosi). Tools: ∞-categories, model categories, simplicial methods. Connects to: topological field theories, enumerative geometry, representation theory.
**Skills Tested:** Derived algebraic geometry, homotopical algebra, moduli problems.

**ID:** AAD-321
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Condensed Mathematics
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain Clausen-Scholze's condensed mathematics and its motivation.
**Expected Answer:** Problem: category of topological abelian groups is not abelian (kernels and cokernels don't behave well). Motivation: do homological algebra with topological groups properly. Condensed mathematics (Clausen-Scholze 2019-): replace topological spaces with "condensed sets" — sheaves on pro-étale site of point (or category of profinite sets). Condensed abelian group: sheaf of abelian groups on this site. Properties: (1) Category Cond(Ab) is abelian, has enough projectives. (2) Forgetful functor Cond(Ab) → Ab is exact. (3) Topological groups embed fully faithfully (for "compactly generated" spaces). (4) Solid modules: further refinement for analytic geometry. Applications: (1) Proper definition of analytic rings. (2) New approach to p-adic geometry (liquid tensor experiment). (3) Simplifies foundations of mathematics involving topology. (4) Connects algebraic and analytic geometry. Controversial: some question if it's "just" a formal trick, others see as foundational breakthrough.
**Skills Tested:** Condensed mathematics, categorical algebra, foundations.

**ID:** AAD-322
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Prismatic Cohomology
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain Bhatt-Scholze's prismatic cohomology and its relation to other cohomology theories.
**Expected Answer:** Prismatic cohomology (Bhatt-Scholze 2019): unified cohomology theory for p-adic varieties, specializing to crystalline, de Rham, and étale cohomology. Setup: prism (A, I) where A is δ-ring (ring with lift of Frobenius) and I ⊂ A is Cartier divisor. Example: (Z_p[[u]], (u)) with δ(u) = 0. For p-adic formal scheme X over O_K: prismatic cohomology Δ_X is complex of modules over prismatic site. Properties: (1) Base change to A/I gives crystalline cohomology. (2) Base change to A gives de Rham cohomology (after derived completion). (3) Inverting certain element gives étale cohomology (via A-and-Ω). (4) Integral theory: works over O_K, not just K. Significance: (1) Unified framework for p-adic Hodge theory. (2) New proofs of comparison theorems. (3) Defines "prismatic F-crystals" (integral p-adic Galois representations). (4) Connects to q-de Rham cohomology, q-Hodge theory. Active research area with many applications.
**Skills Tested:** Prismatic cohomology, p-adic geometry, cohomology theories.

**ID:** AAD-323
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Homotopy Type Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the basic ideas of homotopy type theory (HoTT) and the univalence axiom.
**Expected Answer:** Homotopy type theory: interpretation of Martin-Löf type theory in homotopy theory. Types = spaces, terms = points, equality = path space. Identity type Id_A(x, y) = space of paths from x to y in A. Higher identity types: paths between paths, etc. Types have homotopy type (∞-groupoid). Univalence axiom (Voevodsky): (A ≃ B) ≃ (A =_{U} B) where U is universe. Equivalence of types is same as equality in universe. Consequences: (1) Isomorphic structures are equal (mathematical practice formalized). (2) Equivalence induction: prove property for all types equivalent to A by proving for A. (3) Computational content: univalence has computational interpretation (cubical type theory). Models: simplicial sets (Kan complexes), cubical sets. HoTT as foundation: alternative to set theory, constructive, computer-formalizable (Coq, Agda). Connects: type theory, homotopy theory, category theory, foundations.
**Skills Tested:** Homotopy type theory, univalence axiom, foundations of mathematics.

**ID:** AAD-324
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Cubical Type Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain cubical type theory and how it provides computational content for univalence.
**Expected Answer:** Problem: univalence axiom in HoTT lacks computational interpretation (can't extract program from proof using univalence). Cubical type theory (Cohen, Coquand, Huber, Mörtberg 2017): variant of type theory with computational univalence. Basic idea: add "cube" types I^n (n-dimensional intervals). Terms can depend on interval variables i : I. Path types: Path_A(x, y) = type of terms p(i) with p(0) = x, p(1) = y. Kan composition: fill boxes (open boxes have lids). Univalence computationally: construct explicit equivalence (A ≃ B) → (A = B) using Glue types. Glue [φ ↦ (T, w)] A: type that equals T when φ = 1, equals A when φ = 0. For equivalence e: A ≃ B, glue gives path from A to B in universe. Properties: (1) Can compute with univalent proofs. (2) Retains homotopical interpretation. (3) Implemented in cubical Agda. Significance: makes HoTT practically usable for formalized mathematics.
**Skills Tested:** Cubical type theory, univalence, computational type theory.

**ID:** AAD-325
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Synthetic Differential Geometry
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the basic ideas of synthetic differential geometry (SDG).
**Expected Answer:** SDG: axiomatization of differential geometry using intuitionistic logic and topos theory. Key idea: work in topos where all functions are smooth (no need for smoothness conditions). Basic axioms (Kock-Lawvere): (1) Existence of infinitesimals: object D = {d ∈ R : d² = 0} (non-trivial, d ≠ 0 possible). (2) Kock-Lawvere axiom: for f: R → R and x ∈ R, ∃! f'(x) ∈ R such that f(x+d) = f(x) + f'(x)d for all d ∈ D. Consequences: (1) All functions R → R are differentiable (and smooth). (2) Infinitesimal analysis: derivatives defined by simple algebra. (3) Tangent vectors: maps D → M. (4) Differential forms: maps D^n → R. Models: smooth topos (categories of sheaves on site of smooth manifolds). In these toposes, intuitionistic logic holds (excluded middle fails). Applications: (1) Simplified foundations of differential geometry. (2) Infinitesimal methods made rigorous. (3) Connection to algebraic geometry (formal geometry). (4) Physics: infinitesimal spacetime.
**Skills Tested:** Synthetic differential geometry, topos theory, intuitionistic logic.

**ID:** AAD-326
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Topos Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the concept of a topos and its significance in mathematics.
**Expected Answer:** Topos: category behaving like category of sets. Two types: (1) Grothendieck topos: category of sheaves on site (category with Grothendieck topology). (2) Elementary topos: category with finite limits, power objects (or equivalently, cartesian closed with subobject classifier). Properties of topos E: (1) Has all finite limits and colimits. (2) Cartesian closed: function objects B^A exist. (3) Subobject classifier Ω: monomorphisms A ↪ B classified by maps B → Ω. (4) Internal logic: intuitionistic higher-order logic. Significance: (1) Unified framework: sets, G-sets, sheaves, graphs all form toposes. (2) Geometry: Grothendieck toposes generalize spaces. (3) Logic: models for intuitionistic logic. (4) Foundations: alternative to set theory (elementary toposes as foundations). (5) Algebraic geometry: étale topos, crystalline topos encode geometry. (6) Homotopy theory: ∞-toposes. Examples: Set, Sh(X), PSh(C), G-Set.
**Skills Tested:** Topos theory, category theory, foundations.

**ID:** AAD-327
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Higher Category Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the basic ideas of (∞, 1)-category theory.
**Expected Answer:** (∞, 1)-category: category where morphisms can be composed, and compositions are associative up to coherent higher homotopies. Models: (1) Quasi-categories (Joyal, Lurie): simplicial set satisfying inner horn filling. (2) Complete Segal spaces (Rezk). (3) Simplicial categories (Bergner). (4) Topological categories. Key concepts: (1) Objects, 1-morphisms, 2-morphisms, ... (all invertible above level 1). (2) Mapping spaces: Map(x, y) is space (not just set). (3) Limits/colimits: defined via universal properties in ∞-categorical sense. (4) Adjunctions, monads, etc. generalize. (∞, 1)-category of spaces S: ∞-groupoids. Presentable ∞-categories: generated under colimits by small set. Significance: (1) Derived algebraic geometry. (2) Stable homotopy theory. (3) Topological field theories (Lurie's classification). (4) Higher topos theory. (5) Foundations of homotopy theory. Tools: model categories, ∞-operads, factorization algebras.
**Skills Tested:** Higher category theory, ∞-categories, homotopy theory.

**ID:** AAD-328
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Factorization Homology
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain factorization homology and its relation to topological field theories.
**Expected Answer:** Factorization homology (Ayala, Francis, Lurie): invariant of manifolds with coefficients in E_n-algebras. Setup: M manifold of dimension n, A an E_n-algebra (algebra over little n-disks operad). Factorization homology ∫_M A: computes "configuration space of points in M labeled by A". Properties: (1) Local-to-global: satisfies excision (Mayer-Vietoris). (2) For M = R^n: ∫_{R^n} A = A (by definition). (3) Functorial in M (embedding of manifolds). (4) Computes topological chiral homology. Relation to TFT: (1) Factorization homology constructs n-dimensional TFTs. (2) Assign to M: vector space ∫_M A. (3) Assign to cobordism: linear map. (4) Satisfies Atiyah axioms. Examples: (1) A = E_n-algebra of chains on loop space: recovers string topology. (2) A = factorization algebra of observables: recovers perturbative QFT. (3) A = E_2-algebra: knot invariants. Significance: unified framework for manifold invariants, TQFTs, and algebraic structures.
**Skills Tested:** Factorization homology, topological field theory, higher algebra.

**ID:** AAD-329
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Topological Cyclic Homology
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain topological cyclic homology and its relation to algebraic K-theory.
**Expected Answer:** Algebraic K-theory K(R) of ring R: hard to compute. Topological cyclic homology TC(R): computable approximation. Construction: start with topological Hochschild homology THH(R) (analog of Hochschild homology but using sphere spectrum instead of ground ring). THH has circle action. Define TC as homotopy fixed points of certain operations. Dundas-Goodwillie-McCarthy theorem: relative K-theory K(R) → K(S) maps equivalently to TC(R) → TC(S) (for nilpotent extensions). Trace methods: cyclotomic trace K(R) → TC(R). For p-adic rings: TC computable via syntomic cohomology (Bhatt-Morrow-Scholze). Applications: (1) Compute K-theory of local fields. (2) Prove redshift conjecture (K-theory increases chromatic complexity). (3) Compute K(R) for many rings. Significance: connects algebraic K-theory to chromatic homotopy theory, provides computational tools.
**Skills Tested:** Topological cyclic homology, algebraic K-theory, trace methods.

**ID:** AAD-330
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Chromatic Homotopy Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the chromatic approach to stable homotopy theory.
**Expected Answer:** Stable homotopy theory: study of spectra (generalized cohomology theories). Chromatic approach (Morava, Ravenel, et al): organize spectra by "chromatic level" n ≥ 0. Key concepts: (1) Formal groups: complex oriented cohomology theories E have formal group law F_E over π_*(E). (2) Height: formal group has height n if p^n divides [p]_F but p^{n+1} doesn't. (3) Morava K-theories K(n): field-like spectra with K(n)_* = F_p[v_n, v_n⁻¹], |v_n| = 2(p^n-1). (4) Morava E-theories E(n): Lubin-Tate spectra, E(n)_* = W(F_{p^n})[[u_1, ..., u_{n-1}]][u^{±1}]. Chromatic filtration: spectrum X has tower ... → L_2 X → L_1 X → L_0 X where L_n is Bousfield localization at E(n). Chromatic convergence: X = lim L_n X. Chromatic fracture square: relates L_n X to L_{n-1} X and K(n)-local information. Significance: (1) Organizes stable homotopy category. (2) Computes stable homotopy groups of spheres (chromatic spectral sequence). (3) Connects to formal group theory, number theory.
**Skills Tested:** Chromatic homotopy theory, stable homotopy, formal groups.

**ID:** AAD-331
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Elliptic Cohomology
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain elliptic cohomology and topological modular forms.
**Expected Answer:** Elliptic cohomology: cohomology theory associated to elliptic curves. Elliptic curve E over ring R has formal group of height ≤ 2. Elliptic cohomology theory E with π_*(E) related to modular forms. Topological modular forms tmf: spectrum representing "universal" elliptic cohomology. Construction: Goerss-Hopkins-Miller: sheaf of E_∞-ring spectra O^{top} on moduli stack of elliptic curves M_{ell}. tmf = Γ(M_{ell}, O^{top}). Properties: (1) tmf_* = ring of topological modular forms (related to classical modular forms). (2) tmf detects image of J (stable homotopy). (3) Ando-Hopkins-Rezk: string orientation MString → tmf (analogous to Â-genus MSpin → ko). (4) tmf relates to 2-dimensional conformal field theory (Segal's conjecture). Significance: (1) Connects stable homotopy to modular forms. (2) Computes stable homotopy groups. (3) Geometric perspective on chromatic level 2. (4) Physics: partition functions of 2d CFTs.
**Skills Tested:** Elliptic cohomology, topological modular forms, stable homotopy.

**ID:** AAD-332
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Algebraic K-Theory of Spaces
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain Waldhausen's algebraic K-theory of spaces A(X).
**Expected Answer:** Algebraic K-theory of spaces A(X) (Waldhausen 1985): K-theory of "finite retractive spaces over X". Setup: category R(X) of spaces Y with maps X → Y → X composing to id (retractive spaces over X). Finite: built from X by finitely many cell attachments. A(X) = K(R^{fin}(X)) (Waldhausen K-theory). Properties: (1) A(pt) = K(Z) (algebraic K-theory of integers). (2) Assembly map: X_+ ∧ A(pt) → A(X). (3) Splitting: A(X) ≃ Σ^∞ X_+ ∨ Wh^{Diff}(X) (stable homotopy plus Whitehead space). (4) Wh^{Diff}(X) relates to smooth structures, h-cobordism theorem. (5) Goodwillie calculus: A(X) related to functor X ↦ A(X). Significance: (1) Generalizes algebraic K-theory to spaces. (2) Connects to manifold topology (concordance, pseudoisotopy). (3) Chromatic redshift: A(X) has higher chromatic complexity than X. (4) Trace methods: A(X) → TC(X) (topological cyclic homology).
**Skills Tested:** Algebraic K-theory of spaces, Waldhausen K-theory, manifold topology.

**ID:** AAD-333
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Goodwillie Calculus
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain Goodwillie calculus (calculus of functors).
**Expected Answer:** Goodwillie calculus (Goodwillie 1990s): Taylor tower approximation for functors between ∞-categories. Setup: functor F: C → D (e.g., spaces to spaces). Taylor tower: ... → P_n F → P_{n-1} F → ... → P_0 F where P_n F is "n-excisive" (polynomial of degree ≤ n). Layers: D_n F = fiber(P_n F → P_{n-1} F) (n-th derivative). Properties: (1) D_n F is homogeneous of degree n (like x^n). (2) D_n F classified by symmetric multilinear functor (n-th derivative ∂_n F). (3) Convergence: F ≃ lim P_n F under connectivity assumptions. Examples: (1) F(X) = Σ^∞ Ω^n X: Taylor tower related to stable homotopy. (2) F(X) = A(X) (algebraic K-theory of spaces): layers related to traces. (3) Identity functor: layers are stable homotopy of spheres. Significance: (1) Systematic way to approximate functors. (2) Computes unstable homotopy theory from stable. (3) Connects to manifold calculus (Weiss). (4) Applications to embedding spaces, knot theory.
**Skills Tested:** Goodwillie calculus, functor calculus, homotopy theory.

**ID:** AAD-334
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Manifold Calculus
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain Weiss's manifold calculus and its relation to embedding spaces.
**Expected Answer:** Manifold calculus (Weiss, Goodwillie-Klein): Taylor approximation for functors from manifolds to spaces. Setup: functor F: Man^op → Spaces (contravariant functor from manifolds). Taylor tower: ... → T_n F → T_{n-1} F → ... → T_0 F where T_n F is "polynomial of degree ≤ n" (satisfies inclusion-exclusion for manifolds with ≤ n+1 open subsets). Layers: ∂_n F (n-th derivative) is functor from configuration spaces. Application: embedding spaces. Emb(M, N) = space of embeddings M → N. Functor F(V) = Emb(V, N) for open V ⊂ M. Taylor tower converges if dim N - dim M ≥ 3 (Goodwillie-Klein). T_n F(V) = maps from configuration space Conf_n(V) to Conf_n(N) (with conditions). Layers: sections of bundles over configuration spaces. Significance: (1) Computes embedding spaces from configuration spaces. (2) Proves high-dimensional knot concordance results. (3) Connects to factorization homology. (4) Analogue of Goodwillie calculus for manifolds.
**Skills Tested:** Manifold calculus, embedding spaces, functor calculus.

**ID:** AAD-335
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** String Topology
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain string topology and the Chas-Sullivan loop product.
**Expected Answer:** String topology (Chas-Sullivan 1999): algebraic structures on homology of loop space LM = Map(S¹, M) of manifold M. Key operations: (1) Loop product: H_*(LM) ⊗ H_*(LM) → H_{*+d}(LM) where d = dim M. Defined by intersection of loops: concatenate at basepoint. (2) BV operator: Δ: H_*(LM) → H_{*+1}(LM) from rotating loops. (3) String bracket: makes H_*(LM) into Gerstenhaber algebra. Properties: (1) Loop product is graded-commutative, associative. (2) BV operator squares to 0. (3) H_*(LM) is BV algebra. (4) For simply-connected M: H_*(LM) ≅ HH_*(C^*(M)) (Hochschild homology of cochains). (5) Relates to string field theory (physics). Significance: (1) New invariants of manifolds. (2) Connects to symplectic geometry (Fukaya categories). (3) Generalizes to string operations on higher genus surfaces. (4) Applications to homotopy theory, knot theory.
**Skills Tested:** String topology, loop spaces, algebraic structures.

**ID:** AAD-336
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Factorization Algebras
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain factorization algebras and their relation to quantum field theory.
**Expected Answer:** Factorization algebra (Costello-Gwilliam): algebraic structure encoding observables in QFT. Setup: manifold M. Factorization algebra F: assigns to open U ⊂ M: cochain complex F(U) (observables on U). For disjoint U₁, ..., Uₙ ⊂ V: structure map ⊗ F(Uᵢ) → F(V) (factorization product). Axiom: cosheaf condition (excision). Relation to QFT: (1) F(U) = observables on region U. (2) Factorization = operator product expansion. (3) For M = R: factorization algebra = E₁-algebra (associative). (4) For M = R^n: E_n-algebra. (5) For M = Riemann surface: chiral algebra (Beilinson-Drinfeld). Construction: from Lagrangian field theory via BV formalism. F(U) = BV complex of fields on U. Examples: (1) Free field: F(U) = symmetric algebra on solutions. (2) Chern-Simons: F(U) = Chern-Simons observables. (3) perturbative QFT: factorization algebra of quantum observables. Significance: (1) Rigorous framework for QFT. (2) Connects to factorization homology. (3) Computes partition functions, correlation functions. (4) Relates to vertex algebras, chiral algebras.
**Skills Tested:** Factorization algebras, quantum field theory, algebraic structures.

**ID:** AAD-337
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Topological Chiral Homology
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain topological chiral homology and its relation to factorization homology.
**Expected Answer:** Topological chiral homology (Lurie, Ayala-Francis): generalization of factorization homology to framed manifolds. Setup: M framed n-manifold, A an E_n-algebra. Topological chiral homology ∫_M^⊓ A: computes "configuration space of points in M labeled by A" with framing data. Properties: (1) For M = R^n: ∫_{R^n}^⊓ A = A. (2) Excision: satisfies Mayer-Vietoris. (3) Functorial in framed embeddings. (4) For A = E_n-algebra of chains on based loop space: recovers string topology. Relation to factorization homology: (1) Topological chiral homology = factorization homology for framed manifolds. (2) More generally: factorization homology for manifolds with G-structure (G ⊂ GL_n). (3) Topological chiral homology uses E_n-algebras, factorization homology uses more general coefficient systems. Applications: (1) Construct TQFTs. (2) Compute invariants of manifolds. (3) Relate to higher categories. (4) Connect to representation theory (quantum groups).
**Skills Tested:** Topological chiral homology, factorization homology, TQFT.

**ID:** AAD-338
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Higher Algebra
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain Lurie's higher algebra and its framework.
**Expected Answer:** Higher algebra (Lurie): systematic framework for algebra in ∞-categories. Key concepts: (1) ∞-operads: generalization of operads to ∞-categorical setting. (2) Algebras over ∞-operads: functors satisfying Segal conditions. (3) E_∞-algebras: commutative algebras in ∞-categories. (4) E_n-algebras: algebras over little n-disks operad. (5) Monoidal ∞-categories: ∞-categories with tensor product. (6) Modules, algebras, commutative algebras in monoidal ∞-categories. (7) Stabilization: passage from ∞-categories to stable ∞-categories. (8) Goodwillie calculus in ∞-categorical setting. Applications: (1) Derived algebraic geometry. (2) Topological field theories. (3) Chromatic homotopy theory. (4) Factorization homology. (5) Higher category theory. Significance: (1) Unified framework for algebra and topology. (2) Foundations for modern homotopy theory. (3) Connects algebraic geometry, topology, mathematical physics. (4) Tools for computations in stable homotopy.
**Skills Tested:** Higher algebra, ∞-operads, monoidal ∞-categories.

**ID:** AAD-339
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Spectral Algebraic Geometry
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain spectral algebraic geometry and its relation to derived algebraic geometry.
**Expected Answer:** Spectral algebraic geometry (Lurie): algebraic geometry over E_∞-ring spectra (instead of simplicial commutative rings). Setup: affine spectral scheme Spec A where A is E_∞-ring spectrum. Spectral stack: sheaf of spaces on affine spectral schemes. Relation to derived AG: (1) Derived AG: uses simplicial commutative rings (characteristic 0 or mixed). (2) Spectral AG: uses E_∞-rings (stable homotopy theory). (3) Over Q: equivalent. (4) Over F_p or Z: different (spectral has more structure). Key features: (1) Spectral schemes have "chromatic" structure (height of formal groups). (2) Spectral algebraic K-theory. (3) Topological modular forms tmf as spectral scheme. (4) Deformation theory in spectral setting. Applications: (1) Chromatic homotopy theory. (2) Elliptic cohomology. (3) Topological field theories. (4) Higher algebra. Significance: (1) Geometric perspective on stable homotopy. (2) Connects algebraic geometry to topology. (3) Foundations for modern research.
**Skills Tested:** Spectral algebraic geometry, derived algebraic geometry, E_∞-rings.

**ID:** AAD-340
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Equivariant Homotopy Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain equivariant stable homotopy theory for a finite group G.
**Expected Answer:** Equivariant stable homotopy theory: stable homotopy theory with G-action. G-spectrum: spectrum with G-action (or more precisely, orthogonal G-spectrum). Key concepts: (1) G-representations: real representations V of G. (2) Representation spheres: S^V (one-point compactification). (3) G-stable homotopy category: localization of G-spectra at G-equivariant stable equivalences. (4) Genuine G-spectra: have transfers (norm maps) for all subgroups H ⊂ G. (5) Naive G-spectra: only G-action, no transfers. (6) Geometric fixed points: Φ^H(E) for H ⊂ G. (7) Tom Dieck splitting: π_*(Σ^∞_G X_+) = ⊕_{(H)} π_*(Σ^∞ (X^H / W_G H)_+). Applications: (1) Equivariant cohomology theories. (2) Equivariant K-theory, cobordism. (3) Segal conjecture (proved by Carlsson): completion theorem for A(G). (4) Nilpotence theorem (equivariant version). (5) Chromatic equivariant homotopy. Significance: (1) Richer structure than non-equivariant. (2) Connects to representation theory. (3) Applications to manifold topology (group actions).
**Skills Tested:** Equivariant homotopy theory, G-spectra, equivariant stable homotopy.

**ID:** AAD-341
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Motivic Stable Homotopy Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain motivic stable homotopy theory over a field k.
**Expected Answer:** Motivic stable homotopy theory (Morel-Voevodsky): stable homotopy theory for algebraic varieties over field k. Setup: start with motivic spaces (simplicial presheaves on Sm/k). Stabilize with respect to P¹ = S¹ ∧ G_m (or equivalently, S¹ and G_m). Motivic stable homotopy category SH(k): obtained by inverting P¹. Key features: (1) Bigraded: spheres S^{p,q} = (S¹)^{p-q} ∧ (G_m)^q. (2) Motivic cohomology: H^{p,q}(X, Z) = [X, S^{p,q}]_{SH(k)}. (3) Motivic stable homotopy groups: π_{p,q}(X) = [S^{p,q}, X]. (4) Realization functors: to classical stable homotopy (topological realization), to derived category (Hodge realization). (5) Motivic Adams spectral sequence. Applications: (1) Prove Milnor conjecture (Voevodsky). (2) Compute motivic stable homotopy groups of spheres. (3) Motivic J-homomorphism. (4) Connect to algebraic K-theory. Significance: (1) Algebraic analog of classical stable homotopy. (2) Rich structure (chromatic, etc.). (3) Applications to algebraic geometry, number theory.
**Skills Tested:** Motivic stable homotopy theory, motivic cohomology, stable homotopy.

**ID:** AAD-342
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Equivariant Motivic Homotopy Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain equivariant motivic homotopy theory for a finite group G acting on varieties over k.
**Expected Answer:** Equivariant motivic homotopy theory: combines equivariant and motivic homotopy. Setup: category of G-varieties over k (varieties with G-action). G-motivic spaces: simplicial presheaves on G-smooth varieties. Stabilize with respect to representation spheres: for G-representation V, S^V (one-point compactification). G-motivic stable homotopy category SH_G(k). Key features: (1) Bigraded by representations: S^{V,W} for G-reps V, W. (2) Equivariant motivic cohomology: H^{V,W}_G(X, Z). (3) Geometric fixed points: Φ^H for H ⊂ G. (4) Tom Dieck splitting in motivic setting. (5) Equivariant motivic spectra. Applications: (1) Equivariant algebraic K-theory. (2) Equivariant motivic cohomology operations. (3) Equivariant versions of conjectures (Beilinson, Bloch-Kato). (4) Connect to equivariant derived categories. Significance: (1) Rich structure combining group actions and algebraic geometry. (2) Applications to representation theory, algebraic geometry. (3) Active research area.
**Skills Tested:** Equivariant motivic homotopy, equivariant algebraic geometry, stable homotopy.

**ID:** AAD-343
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Derived Categories of Coherent Sheaves
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the derived category D^b(Coh(X)) for a smooth projective variety X and its role in modern algebraic geometry.
**Expected Answer:** D^b(Coh(X)): bounded derived category of coherent sheaves on X. Objects: bounded complexes of coherent sheaves. Morphisms: chain maps localized at quasi-isomorphisms. Properties: (1) Triangulated category (distinguished triangles from mapping cones). (2) Serre functor: S(F) = F ⊗ ω_X[dim X] (ω_X = canonical bundle). (3) Semi-orthogonal decompositions: D^b(Coh(X)) = ⟨A₁, ..., Aₙ⟩. (4) Exceptional collections: sequence of objects E₁, ..., Eₙ with Hom(Eᵢ, Eⱼ[k]) = 0 for i > j or k ≠ 0, and generate D^b(Coh(X)). (5) Fourier-Mukai transforms: equivalences D^b(Coh(X)) ≅ D^b(Coh(Y)) given by kernel P ∈ D^b(Coh(X × Y)). Role: (1) Bondal-Orlov: D^b(Coh(X)) determines X (for varieties with ample or anti-ample canonical bundle). (2) Homological mirror symmetry (Kontsevich): D^b(Coh(X)) ≅ Fukaya category of mirror. (3) Bridgeland stability conditions. (4) Categorical resolutions of singularities.
**Skills Tested:** Derived categories, coherent sheaves, algebraic geometry.

**ID:** AAD-344
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Stability Conditions on Triangulated Categories
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain Bridgeland stability conditions on triangulated categories.
**Expected Answer:** Bridgeland stability condition (Bridgeland 2007) on triangulated category D: pair σ = (Z, P) where (1) Z: K(D) → C is group homomorphism (central charge). (2) P(φ) ⊂ D for φ ∈ R (semistable objects of phase φ). Axioms: (1) Z(E) ∈ {re^{πiφ} : r > 0} for E ∈ P(φ). (2) P(φ+1) = P(φ)[1]. (3) If φ₁ > φ₂, then Hom(E₁, E₂) = 0 for Eᵢ ∈ P(φᵢ). (4) Harder-Narasimhan: every E has filtration with semistable factors of decreasing phase. (5) Support property: Z bounded on certain lattice. Properties: (1) Space of stability conditions Stab(D) is complex manifold. (2) Autoequivalences act on Stab(D). (3) Wall-crossing: as σ varies, moduli spaces of σ-stable objects change. Applications: (1) D^b(Coh(X)) for surfaces: construct stability conditions. (2) Counting invariants (Donaldson-Thomas, Pandharipande-Thomas). (3) Mirror symmetry (stability conditions on Fukaya category). (4) Categorical Donaldson-Thomas theory.
**Skills Tested:** Stability conditions, triangulated categories, moduli problems.

**ID:** AAD-345
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Noncommutative Algebraic Geometry
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the basic ideas of noncommutative algebraic geometry.
**Expected Answer:** Noncommutative algebraic geometry: study "noncommutative spaces" via their categories of sheaves. Basic idea: space X determined by category Coh(X) (or D^b(Coh(X))). Define "noncommutative space" by specifying abstract triangulated category (or abelian category). Examples: (1) Noncommutative projective space: category of graded modules over quantum polynomial ring. (2) Noncommutative resolutions: D^b(Coh(Y)) for resolution Y → X embedded in D^b(mod-A) for noncommutative A. (3) Matrix factorizations: category of matrix factorizations of potential W (Landau-Ginzburg models). (4) Categories from quivers with relations. Tools: (1) Derived categories, dg-categories. (2) Hochschild (co)homology (noncommutative differential forms). (3) Cyclic homology (noncommutative de Rham). (4) K-theory. Applications: (1) Homological mirror symmetry. (2) Noncommutative crepant resolutions. (3) Categorical Donaldson-Thomas theory. (4) Representation theory (quiver varieties).
**Skills Tested:** Noncommutative geometry, derived categories, dg-categories.

**ID:** AAD-346
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:**dg-Categories and A-infinity Categories
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain dg-categories and A_∞-categories and their role in modern mathematics.
**Expected Answer:** dg-category: category enriched over chain complexes. Objects, morphism complexes Hom(A, B) with differential d, composition chain map. A_∞-category: generalization where associativity holds up to coherent homotopy. Operations m_n: Hom(A_{n-1}, A_n) ⊗ ... ⊗ Hom(A₀, A₁) → Hom(A₀, A_n) of degree 2-n satisfying A_∞-relations. Relation: dg-category = A_∞-category with m_n = 0 for n ≥ 3. Homotopy category H⁰(C): objects same, morphisms H⁰(Hom(A, B)). Role: (1) Derived categories: D(A) = H⁰(dg-category of complexes). (2) Fukaya category: A_∞-category (composition = counting holomorphic disks). (3) Category of modules: dg-functors C^{op} → Ch. (4) Yoneda embedding: C → Mod-C (fully faithful). (5) Quasi-equivalences: morphisms inducing equivalences on H⁰. Applications: (1) Derived algebraic geometry. (2) Homological mirror symmetry. (3) Noncommutative geometry. (4) Topological field theories.
**Skills Tested:** dg-categories, A_∞-categories, enriched category theory.

**ID:** AAD-347
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Topological K-Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain topological K-theory and Bott periodicity.
**Expected Answer:** Topological K-theory: generalized cohomology theory. K⁰(X) = Grothendieck group of vector bundles over X. K⁻ⁿ(X) = K⁰(Σⁿ X) (reduced K-theory of n-fold suspension). Bott periodicity: K^{-n-2}(X) ≅ K^{-n}(X) (complex K-theory). Equivalently: Ω² BU × Z ≃ BU × Z (loop space). Real K-theory KO: Bott periodicity KO^{-n-8} ≅ KO^{-n}. Properties: (1) Multiplicative: K*(X) ⊗ K*(Y) → K*(X × Y). (2) Chern character: ch: K*(X) ⊗ Q → H^{even}(X; Q) (isomorphism rationally). (3) Thom isomorphism: K*(X) ≅ K*(Th(ξ)) for Spin^c bundle ξ. (4) Atiyah-Singer index theorem: index(D) ∈ K*(pt) = Z. Applications: (1) Vector field problem (Adams): max number of linearly independent vector fields on S^{n-1}. (2) J-homomorphism π_k(O) → π_k^s. (3) Adams operations ψ^k. (4) K-theoretic obstruction theory. Significance: (1) First generalized cohomology theory. (2) Connects topology, geometry, analysis. (3) Foundation for other cohomology theories.
**Skills Tested:** Topological K-theory, Bott periodicity, vector bundles.

**ID:** AAD-348
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Cobordism Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain cobordism theory and the Thom spectrum MO.
**Expected Answer:** Cobordism: manifolds M, N are cobordant if ∃ W with ∂W = M ⊔ N. Cobordism ring Ω_*: graded ring under disjoint union and cartesian product. Thom's theorem: Ω_*^O ≅ π_*(MO) where MO is Thom spectrum. MO = colim Σ^{-n} Th(γ_n) where γ_n is universal bundle over BO(n). Properties: (1) π_*(MO) = polynomial ring over F_2 with generators in each degree ≠ 2^k - 1. (2) MO represents unoriented cobordism: MO^*(X) = unoriented cobordism of maps to X. (3) MU (complex cobordism): π_*(MU) = Lazard ring (classifies formal group laws). (4) MSO (oriented): π_*(MSO) ⊗ Q = polynomial ring. (5) MSpin, MString, etc. Applications: (1) Classification of manifolds up to cobordism. (2) Characteristic numbers (Pontryagin, Stiefel-Whitney). (3) Complex cobordism MU: universal complex-oriented cohomology theory. (4) Chromatic homotopy theory (MU → E(n) → K(n)). Significance: (1) Foundation for stable homotopy theory. (2) Connects to formal groups, algebraic geometry.
**Skills Tested:** Cobordism theory, Thom spectra, stable homotopy.

**ID:** AAD-349
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Stable Homotopy Theory — Spectra
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the category of spectra and its role in stable homotopy theory.
**Expected Answer:** Spectra: objects representing generalized cohomology theories. Definition (modern): symmetric spectrum = sequence of spaces E_n with S¹ ∧ E_n → E_{n+1} (or orthogonal spectrum using inner product spaces). Stable homotopy category: localization of spectra at stable equivalences (maps inducing isomorphisms on stable homotopy groups). Properties: (1) Triangulated category (distinguished triangles from cofiber sequences). (2) Symmetric monoidal (smash product E ∧ F). (3) Compact objects: finite spectra. (4) Brown representability: cohomology theories represented by spectra. Key spectra: (1) Sphere spectrum S: π_*(S) = stable homotopy groups of spheres. (2) Eilenberg-MacLane spectra HA: represent ordinary cohomology. (3) K-theory spectra KU, KO. (4) Thom spectra MO, MU. (5) Moore spectra, etc. Applications: (1) Stable homotopy groups of spheres (hard to compute). (2) Chromatic homotopy theory. (3) Algebraic K-theory. (4) Topological field theories. Significance: (1) Foundation for stable homotopy. (2) Connects topology, algebra, geometry.
**Skills Tested:** Spectra, stable homotopy theory, generalized cohomology.

**ID:** AAD-350
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Stable Homotopy Groups of Spheres
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the computation of stable homotopy groups of spheres π_n^s and key results.
**Expected Answer:** π_n^s = colim_k π_{n+k}(S^k) (stable homotopy groups of spheres). Computed via: (1) Adams spectral sequence: E₂ = Ext_A(H*(S; F_p), F_p) ⇒ π_*(S) ⊗ Z_p. (2) Adams-Novikov spectral sequence: uses MU instead of H. (3) Chromatic spectral sequence: organize by height. Key results: (1) π_0^s = Z (degree). (2) π_1^s = Z/2 (η = Hopf map). (3) π_2^s = Z/2 (η²). (4) π_3^s = Z/24 (ν, related to quaternionic Hopf map). (5) π_4^s = 0. (6) Finite in each degree (Serre). (7) Image of J: cyclic summands from J-homomorphism π_k(O) → π_k^s (Adams). (8) Nilpotence theorem (Nishida): positive degree elements are nilpotent. (9) Chromatic redshift: K(π_n^s) has higher chromatic complexity. Significance: (1) Fundamental computation in topology. (2) Connects to geometry (framed manifolds via Pontryagin-Thom). (3) Active research (computations to high stems).
**Skills Tested:** Stable homotopy groups, spectral sequences, chromatic homotopy.

**ID:** AAD-351
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Operads and Algebras over Operads
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain operads and algebras over operads.
**Expected Answer:** Operad O: collection of spaces O(n) (n-ary operations) with composition and symmetric group action. Axioms: associativity, unit, equivariance. Examples: (1) End_X: O(n) = Hom(X^{⊗n}, X) for object X in symmetric monoidal category. (2) Assoc: O(n) = Σ_n (symmetric group). (3) Comm: O(n) = *. (4) Lie: O(n) from Lie bracket operations. (5) E_n: O(n) = configuration space of n points in R^n (little n-disks operad). Algebra over operad O: object A with maps O(n) ⊗ A^{⊗n} → A satisfying axioms. Examples: (1) Assoc-algebra = associative algebra. (2) Comm-algebra = commutative algebra. (3) E_n-algebra = algebra over little n-disks (for n=1: A_∞-algebra, n=∞: E_∞-algebra = commutative up to coherent homotopy). Applications: (1) Deformation theory (Kontsevich). (2) Topological field theories. (3) Factorization homology. (4) Higher algebra (Lurie). (5) String topology. Significance: (1) Encodes operations and relations. (2) Unified framework for algebraic structures. (3) Homotopy theory (∞-operads).
**Skills Tested:** Operads, algebras over operads, higher algebra.

**ID:** AAD-352
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Higher Topos Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain Lurie's higher topos theory.
**Expected Answer:** Higher topos theory (Lurie): ∞-categorical generalization of topos theory. ∞-topos: presentable ∞-category satisfying Giraud axioms (or equivalently, left exact localization of PSh(C) for small ∞-category C). Properties: (1) Has all small limits and colimits. (2) Universal colimits (pullback of colimit is colimit). (3) Effective epimorphisms (groupoid objects effective). (4) Internal logic: higher categorical version of intuitionistic logic. Examples: (1) Sh_∞(X): ∞-topos of sheaves of spaces on space X. (2) PSh_∞(C): presheaves on ∞-category. (3) Etale ∞-topos of scheme. Key concepts: (1) Objects: ∞-sheaves (satisfy descent). (2) Morphisms: natural transformations. (3) Geometric morphisms: adjunctions between ∞-toposes. (4) Points of ∞-topos. Applications: (1) Derived algebraic geometry. (2) Elliptic cohomology (tmf as sheaf of E_∞-rings on M_{ell}). (3) Topological field theories. (4) Homotopy type theory (models). Significance: (1) Foundation for modern homotopy theory. (2) Connects topology, geometry, logic.
**Skills Tested:** Higher topos theory, ∞-toposes, higher category theory.

**ID:** AAD-353
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Factorization Homology — Applications
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain applications of factorization homology to topological field theories and knot invariants.
**Expected Answer:** Factorization homology ∫_M A constructs TQFTs and knot invariants. TQFTs: (1) Assign to n-manifold M: vector space ∫_M A. (2) Assign to cobordism W: linear map ∫_W A. (3) Satisfies Atiyah axioms (functorial, monoidal). Examples: (1) A = E_n-algebra of chains on loop space: ∫_M A = string topology of M. (2) A = E_2-algebra: 2-dimensional TQFT. (3) A = factorization algebra: perturbative QFT. Knot invariants: (1) Knot K ⊂ R³: ∫_{R³ \ K} A (complement). (2) A = E_2-algebra from quantum group: recovers Jones polynomial, HOMFLY-PT. (3) A = E_n-algebra: higher-dimensional knot invariants. Properties: (1) Local-to-global: compute from pieces. (2) Functorial: embeddings of manifolds induce maps. (3) Relates to configuration spaces. Significance: (1) Unified framework for manifold invariants. (2) Connects TQFT, knot theory, representation theory. (3) Computational tool.
**Skills Tested:** Factorization homology, TQFT, knot invariants.

**ID:** AAD-354
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Topological Field Theory — Extended TQFT
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain extended topological field theories and the Baez-Dolan cobordism hypothesis.
**Expected Answer:** Extended TQFT: TQFT assigns data to manifolds of all codimensions. n-dimensional extended TQFT: symmetric monoidal functor Z: Bord_n^{fr} → C where C is symmetric monoidal (∞, n)-category. Assigns: (n-k)-manifold: object in C, codimension-k bordism: k-morphism. Cobordism hypothesis (Baez-Dolan, proved by Lurie): fully extended n-dimensional framed TQFTs classified by fully dualizable objects in C with homotopy fixed point for O(n)-action. Fully dualizable: object X with duals at all levels (adjoints at all levels). For C = n-Vect: fully dualizable = finite-dimensional vector space. For C = n-Cat: fully dualizable = fully dualizable n-category. Applications: (1) Classification of TQFTs. (2) Construct TQFTs from algebraic data. (3) Reshetikhin-Turaev TQFTs from modular tensor categories. (4) Crane-Yetter, Barrett-Westbury TQFTs. Significance: (1) Deep connection between topology and higher algebra. (2) Foundation for modern TQFT. (3) Applications to condensed matter physics.
**Skills Tested:** Extended TQFT, cobordism hypothesis, higher categories.

**ID:** AAD-355
**Category:** Mathematics
**Subcategory:** Factorization Algebras — Quantum Field Theory
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain how factorization algebras provide a rigorous framework for perturbative quantum field theory.
