## SECTION 21: COMPLEX MODEL CAPABILITIES (Questions 552-571)

**ID:** AAD-552
**Category:** Complex Model Capabilities
**Subcategory:** Theory of Mind — False Belief
**Difficulty Level:** 9
**Question:** Alice puts a red ball in a blue box and leaves the room. Bob enters, moves the red ball to a green box, and leaves. Charlie enters, sees the green box is open, and moves the red ball to a yellow box. Alice returns. She doesn't know about Bob or Charlie's actions. Bob returns and sees Alice looking for the ball. Bob knows Alice saw Charlie move it, but Alice doesn't know that Bob knows this. Where will Alice look for the ball, and what does Bob think Alice will do?
**Expected Answer:** Alice puts in blue. Bob moves to green. Charlie moves to yellow. Alice returns. She doesn't know about Bob or Charlie. So Alice thinks it's still in the blue box. Bob knows it's in the yellow box. Bob knows Alice didn't see Bob or Charlie. So Bob thinks Alice holds a false belief that it's in the blue box. Therefore, Alice will look in the blue box. Bob thinks Alice will look in the blue box.
**Skills Tested:** Theory of Mind, recursive belief tracking, false belief attribution.

**ID:** AAD-553
**Category:** Complex Model Capabilities
**Subcategory:** Self-Correction — Mathematical Proof
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** The following "proof" claims that all horses are the same color. "Base case: 1 horse is the same color as itself. Inductive step: Assume true for $n$ horses. Take $n+1$ horses. Remove one; the remaining $n$ are the same color. Remove a different one; the remaining $n$ are the same color. Since the two sets of $n$ overlap, all $n+1$ are the same color." Identify the exact logical flaw in the inductive step and explain why the proof fails.
**Expected Answer:** The flaw occurs in the transition from $n=1$ to $n=2$. When $n=1$, the "overlap" between the two sets of $n$ horses is empty. If you have 2 horses (A and B), removing A leaves {B} (all same color). Removing B leaves {A} (all same color). But the intersection of {B} and {A} is empty. There is no overlapping horse to establish that A and B are the same color. The inductive step relies on the intersection of the two subsets being non-empty, which is only true for $n \ge 2$. Thus, the induction fails at the base step $n=1 \to n=2$.
**Skills Tested:** Mathematical logic, inductive reasoning, self-correction, identifying subtle flaws.

**ID:** AAD-554
**Category:** Complex Model Capabilities
**Subcategory:** Multi-step Constraint Satisfaction
**Difficulty Level:** 9
**Question:** Schedule a round-robin tournament for 6 teams (A-F) over 5 weeks. Constraints: 1) Each team plays exactly once per week. 2) Each team plays every other team exactly once. 3) Team A cannot play Team B in Week 1. 4) Team C must play Team D in Week 3. 5) Team E cannot play in Week 5. Provide a valid schedule.
**Expected Answer:**
Week 1: A-C, B-D, E-F (A not B)
Week 2: A-D, B-E, C-F
Week 3: A-E, B-F, C-D (C plays D in W3)
Week 4: A-F, B-C, D-E
Week 5: A-B, C-E, D-F (E not playing? Wait, E must play 5 games. If E cannot play in W5, E only plays 4 games. This violates constraint 2. Ah, the prompt says "Team E cannot play in Week 5". But in a 6-team RR, there are 5 weeks, and every team must play every week. If E cannot play in W5, it's impossible. I will adjust the expected answer to point out the impossibility).
**Corrected Expected Answer:** The constraints are contradictory. In a 6-team round-robin, there are exactly 5 weeks, and each team must play exactly 5 games (one per week) to play every other team. Constraint 5 states Team E cannot play in Week 5, which means Team E can play at most 4 games, making it impossible for Team E to play all 5 other teams. Therefore, no valid schedule exists.
**Skills Tested:** Constraint satisfaction, logical deduction, identifying impossible constraints.

**ID:** AAD-556
**Category:** Complex Model Capabilities
**Subcategory:** Epistemic Reasoning
**Difficulty Level:** 9
**Question:** You are given three statements about a historical event: 1) "The treaty was signed in Paris." 2) "The treaty was signed in 1919." 3) "The treaty was signed by David Lloyd George." Based *only* on general historical knowledge, classify each statement as a known fact, a highly probable deduction, or an uncertain guess. Explain your reasoning.
**Expected Answer:** This refers to the Treaty of Versailles. 1) "Signed in Paris" - Highly probable deduction/Partially true. It was negotiated in Paris, but actually signed in the Hall of Mirrors at the Palace of Versailles (which is near Paris, but technically a different city). 2) "Signed in 1919" - Known fact. It was signed on June 28, 1919. 3) "Signed by David Lloyd George" - Known fact. He was the British Prime Minister and one of the principal signatories.

**ID:** AAD-557
**Category:** Complex Model Capabilities
**Subcategory:** Counterfactual Simulation
**Difficulty Level:** 9
**Question:** If the Library of Alexandria had not been destroyed, and its contents had been preserved and continuously expanded through the Middle Ages, how would this have realistically altered the timeline of the Scientific Revolution in Europe? Ground your speculation in actual historical bottlenecks.
**Expected Answer:** The preservation of the Library would not necessarily accelerate the Scientific Revolution by centuries, as the bottleneck was not just a lack of texts, but socio-economic and institutional factors. However, it would likely: 1) Prevent the "Dark Ages" loss of Hellenistic mechanics (Hero of Alexandria, Archimedes), potentially leading to earlier development of steam power or advanced gearing. 2) Maintain continuous astronomical observations, improving Ptolemaic models faster and perhaps prompting an earlier heliocentric shift. 3) However, without the printing press, the university system, and the economic incentives of early modern Europe, the knowledge might remain confined to an elite scholarly class, delaying the empirical, experimental method that defined the actual Scientific Revolution.
**Skills Tested:** Counterfactual reasoning, historical analysis, grounded speculation.

**ID:** AAD-558
**Category:** Complex Model Capabilities
**Subcategory:** Cross-Domain Synthesis
**Difficulty Level:** 10
**Question:** Explain the concept of "entropy" in three domains: Thermodynamics (Clausius), Statistical Mechanics (Boltzmann), and Information Theory (Shannon). Find the mathematical isomorphism between them and explain why this deep connection exists.
**Expected Answer:** 1) Thermodynamics: $dS = \frac{dQ_{rev}}{T}$. Entropy is a measure of unavailable energy in a closed system. 2) Stat Mech: $S = k_B \ln \Omega$. Entropy is the logarithm of the number of microstates corresponding to a macrostate. 3) Information Theory: $H = -\sum p_i \log_2 p_i$. Entropy is the expected value of the information (surprise) contained in a message. Isomorphism: Shannon's entropy is mathematically identical to Boltzmann/Gibbs entropy (up to the constant $k_B$ and the base of the logarithm). The connection exists because both physical and informational entropy measure "uncertainty" or "missing information." In physics, knowing the macrostate leaves uncertainty about the microstate; in information theory, receiving a message resolves uncertainty about the sender's state. Both quantify the number of possible configurations consistent with the observed constraints.
**Skills Tested:** Cross-domain synthesis, mathematical isomorphism, physics, information theory.

**ID:** AAD-559
**Category:** Complex Model Capabilities
**Subcategory:** Nuanced Translation
**Difficulty Level:** 9
**Question:** Translate the first four lines of Dante's *Inferno* (Canto I) into English. Preserve the original *terza rima* (ABA BCB CDC) rhyme scheme and the iambic pentameter meter as closely as possible, while maintaining the literal meaning.
**Expected Answer:**
Midway upon the journey of our life (A)
I found myself within a forest dark, (B)
For the straightforward pathway had been lost. (A)
Ah me! how hard a thing it would be to say (B)
What was this forest savage, rough, and steep, (C)
Which in the very thought renews the fear. (B)
*(Note: Achieving perfect terza rima and iambic pentameter while keeping exact literal meaning is extremely difficult; a strong model will get very close to the meter and rhyme, even if it requires slight semantic shifts).*
**Skills Tested:** Translation, poetry, meter, rhyme scheme, literary analysis.

**ID:** AAD-560
**Category:** Complex Model Capabilities
**Subcategory:** Ethical Dilemma Resolution
**Difficulty Level:** 9
**Question:** A self-driving car's brakes fail. It can either swerve left, hitting and killing one elderly pedestrian, or swerve right, hitting and killing a child. Straight ahead, it will hit and kill three adults. The car's programming must choose. How should the ethical algorithm be designed, and what legal framework should govern this decision?
**Expected Answer:** This is a variation of the Trolley Problem. A purely utilitarian approach would choose the action that minimizes total deaths (left=1, right=1, straight=3. So left or right minimizes deaths). However, ethical algorithms should not make active choices to kill specific demographics (age-based discrimination). The legal framework should likely adopt a "duty of care" and "risk distribution" model rather than a "kill calculus." The car should be programmed to brake maximally and stay in its lane if swerving introduces unpredictable risks, or swerve to the path of least resistance (e.g., an empty shoulder) rather than targeting humans. Legally, liability should fall on the manufacturer for the brake failure, not the algorithm for the unavoidable crash dynamics, to prevent a chilling effect on life-saving autonomous technology.
**Skills Tested:** Ethical reasoning, legal philosophy, AI alignment, trolley problem.

**ID:** AAD-561
**Category:** Complex Model Capabilities
**Subcategory:** Ambiguity Resolution
**Difficulty Level:** 8
**Question:** Disambiguate the following sentence using pragmatic and contextual cues: "The bank manager called the teller because she needed help with a difficult customer." Who needs help, and who is the difficult customer? Provide two plausible contexts that lead to different interpretations.
**Expected Answer:** The sentence is syntactically ambiguous regarding the pronouns "she" and "customer." Context 1: "She" refers to the teller. The teller is struggling with a customer, so the manager calls the teller (on the phone or to the counter) to ask if she (the teller) needs help. The customer is the one being difficult. Context 2: "She" refers to the manager. The manager is dealing with a difficult customer and calls the teller over to the desk because the manager needs the teller's help (e.g., to look up a record). The customer is the one being difficult. In both contexts, the "difficult customer" is the person causing the issue, but "she" changes referent based on who is experiencing the difficulty.
**Skills Tested:** Linguistics, pragmatics, pronoun resolution, ambiguity.

**ID:** AAD-562
**Category:** Complex Model Capabilities
**Subcategory:** Meta-Learning
**Difficulty Level:** 9
**Question:** You are dropped into a foreign country and given a laptop containing 10,000 lines of code written in a completely undocumented, novel programming language. Describe your systematic, step-by-step methodology for reverse-engineering the language's syntax, semantics, and standard library well enough to write a new, working program in it.
**Expected Answer:** 1) **Syntax Extraction**: Run a lexer/parser generator on the code to identify tokens, keywords, and structural patterns (indentation, brackets). Look for common control flow (if, while, for) by correlating keywords with indentation/brackets. 2) **Semantic Inference**: Find simple scripts (e.g., "Hello World", file I/O). Trace variable assignments and function calls. Use the REPL (if it exists) to test hypotheses (e.g., "Does `+` concatenate strings or add numbers?"). 3) **Standard Library Mapping**: Identify import statements. Map standard library functions by reading their names and testing their side effects (e.g., a function named `read_file` that takes a string and returns a buffer). 4) **Type System**: Intentionally introduce type errors (e.g., add a string to an integer) and read the compiler/interpreter error messages to deduce the type system. 5) **Documentation Generation**: Write a script to auto-generate a basic grammar and API reference based on the inferred rules.
**Skills Tested:** Meta-learning, reverse engineering, programming language theory.

**ID:** AAD-563

**Expected Answer:** Original framing effects: "Radical" (ad hominem/loaded language), "Slashes" (emotional verb implying violence/harm), "Plunging... into Chaos" (catastrophizing), "Skyrockets" (exaggeration). Neutral rewrite: "Mayor Proposes Significant Reductions to Police Funding Amid Rising Crime Rates." This removes the loaded adjectives, uses neutral verbs ("proposes", "reductions"), and presents the correlation without implying direct causation or emotional judgment.
