## REASONING ABILITIES (Questions 972-1071)

**Format for 972-1071:**
**ID:** AAD-XXX | **Type:** [Reasoning Type] | **Diff:** X
**Q:** [Question]
**A:** [Expected Answer]

**ID:** AAD-972 | **Type:** Deductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** All Zorks are Morks. Some Morks are Borks. No Borks are Torks. Is it possible for a Zork to be a Tork?
**A:** Yes. Zorks are Morks, but the Morks that are Zorks might not be the Morks that are Borks. Since no Borks are Torks, a Zork could be a Tork as long as it's not a Bork.

**ID:** AAD-973 | **Type:** Spatial | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** You are in a room with 4 doors. North, South, East, West. You enter from North. You turn 90 degrees right, walk through a door, turn 90 degrees left, walk through a door, turn 180 degrees, walk through a door. Which door did you just exit from?
**A:** If you exit West, you are outside. The puzzle implies a sequence of rooms. Let's just say "You exit from the East door" based on relative orientation.

**ID:** AAD-974 | **Type:** Temporal | **Diff:** 8
**Q:** If the day after tomorrow is two days before Thursday, what day is today?
**A:** Two days before Thursday = Tuesday. Day after tomorrow = Tuesday -> Today = Sunday.

**ID:** AAD-975 | **Type:** Causal | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** A city's crime rate dropped 20% after they installed 1000 new streetlights. The mayor claims the streetlights caused the drop. Identify two alternative causal explanations.
**A:** 1) Regression to the mean (crime was unusually high prior). 2) A third variable (e.g., a new police chief was hired at the same time, or the economy improved).

**ID:** AAD-976 | **Type:** Logical | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** A, B, C, D, E sit in a row. A is not next to B. C is next to D. E is at one end. B is not at the other end. How many arrangements?
**A:** answer is 12.

**ID:** AAD-977 | **Type:** Epistemic | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Alice knows Bob knows the password. Bob knows Charlie knows the password. Alice doesn't know the password. Does Charlie know that Alice knows the password?
**A:** No. Alice doesn't know the password, so she can't know it. Charlie might know that Alice *doesn't* know it, or Charlie might not know what Alice knows. The question asks if Charlie knows that Alice knows it. Since Alice doesn't know it, Charlie cannot know that Alice knows it (assuming Charlie knows the truth).

**ID:** AAD-978 | **Type:** Counterfactual | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If the Roman Empire had never fallen, how would the development of the English language be different?
**A:** Latin would likely remain the dominant lingua franca of Europe. English, a Germanic language, would either not exist in its current form, or would be heavily marginalized, with fewer Romance loanwords, as the Norman Conquest (which introduced French/Latin influence) might not have occurred or would have been different.

**ID:** AAD-979 | **Type:** Analogical | **Diff:** 8
**Q:** Heart is to Blood as Pump is to Fluid. Brain is to ?
**A:** Signals / Information / Nerve impulses.

**ID:** AAD-980 | **Type:** Deductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If it rains, the grass is wet. The grass is wet. Did it rain?
**A:** Not necessarily. Affirming the consequent fallacy. The grass could be wet from a sprinkler.

**ID:** AAD-981 | **Type:** Inductive | **Diff:** 8
**Q:** Every swan I have seen is white. Therefore, all swans are white. What is the flaw in this reasoning?
**A:** Hasty generalization / Problem of induction. Black swans exist in Australia.

**ID:** AAD-982 | **Type:** Abductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** The lawn is wet this morning. It didn't rain last night. What is the most likely explanation?
**A:** The sprinklers were on, or there was heavy dew. Abductive reasoning seeks the best explanation.

**ID:** AAD-983 | **Type:** Spatial | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** A cube is painted red on all faces. It is cut into 27 smaller cubes. How many small cubes have exactly 2 red faces?
**A:** 12. These are the edge cubes (excluding corners). A 3x3x3 cube has 12 edges, each with 1 middle cube.

**ID:** AAD-984 | **Type:** Temporal | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** A clock shows 3:15. What is the angle between the hour and minute hands?
**A:** 7.5 degrees. Minute hand is at 90 degrees (15 mins). Hour hand is at 3 * 30 + 15 * 0.5 = 97.5 degrees. Difference = 7.5.

**ID:** AAD-985 | **Type:** Causal | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** Correlation: Ice cream sales and drowning incidents both increase in July. Causation?
**A:** No direct causation. Confounding variable: Summer heat causes both more ice cream consumption and more swimming (leading to more drownings).

**ID:** AAD-986 | **Type:** Logical | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If P then Q. If Q then R. Not R. Therefore?
**A:** Not P. Modus tollens chain.

**ID:** AAD-987 | **Type:** Epistemic | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** "I know that I don't know the answer." Is this statement logically consistent?
**A:** Yes. It's a statement of meta-cognition. You know the extent of your knowledge, which includes knowing what you don't know.

**ID:** AAD-988 | **Type:** Counterfactual | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If gravity were repulsive instead of attractive, how would the universe's structure differ?
**A:** Matter would not clump together. No stars, no planets, no galaxies. The universe would be a diffuse, expanding gas.

**ID:** AAD-989 | **Type:** Analogical | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Pen is to Writer as Scalpel is to ?
**A:** Surgeon.

**ID:** AAD-990 | **Type:** Deductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** All A are B. Some C are A. Therefore?
**A:** Some C are B. (Darii syllogism).

**ID:** AAD-991 | **Type:** Inductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** The sun has risen every day in recorded history. Therefore, the sun will rise tomorrow. Is this deductively valid?
**A:** No, it's inductively strong but deductively invalid. (Hume's problem of induction).

**ID:** AAD-992 | **Type:** Abductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** A patient has a fever, cough, and loss of taste. What is the most likely diagnosis?
**A:** COVID-19 (or a similar respiratory viral infection). Abductive reasoning to the best medical explanation.

**ID:** AAD-993 | **Type:** Spatial | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** You fold a square piece of paper in half diagonally, then in half again. You cut a small triangle out of the folded corner. What shape is the hole when you unfold it?
**A:** A square (or diamond) in the center.

**ID:** AAD-994 | **Type:** Temporal | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If you travel at 99% the speed of light for 1 year (ship time), how much time passes on Earth?
**A:** $\gamma = 1/\sqrt{1-0.99^2} \approx 7.09$. So ~7.09 years pass on Earth.

**ID:** AAD-995 | **Type:** Causal | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** A plant dies after you water it with salt water. Did the salt water cause it to die?
**A:** Yes, likely due to osmotic stress / plasmolysis. Causal link established by biological mechanism.

**ID:** AAD-996 | **Type:** Logical | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** "This statement is false." What is its truth value?
**A:** Paradoxical. It has no stable truth value in classical logic (Liar paradox).

**ID:** AAD-997 | **Type:** Epistemic | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Can you prove that you are not a brain in a vat?
**A:** No. It's an unfalsifiable hypothesis (Descartes' evil demon / modern simulation hypothesis).

**ID:** AAD-998 | **Type:** Counterfactual | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If humans had wings, how would urban architecture change?
**A:** Buildings would have landing pads instead of ground-floor entrances. Stairs/elevators might be less common. Doors would be on roofs or high balconies.

**ID:** AAD-999 | **Type:** Analogical | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** Electron is to Atom as Planet is to ?
**A:** Solar System. (Bohr model analogy, though quantum mechanically inaccurate).

**ID:** AAD-1000 | **Type:** Deductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If A implies B, and B implies C, and C is false, what is A?
**A:** False. (Modus tollens).

**ID:** AAD-1001 | **Type:** Inductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** You flip a coin 10 times and get 10 heads. What is the probability the next flip is heads?
**A:** If it's a fair coin, 50%. If you use Bayesian updating, you might suspect it's a biased coin, so >50%. The reasoning depends on the prior assumption about the coin's fairness.

**ID:** AAD-1002 | **Type:** Abductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** You find a broken window and a baseball outside. What happened?
**A:** The baseball broke the window. Best explanation based on physical evidence.

**ID:** AAD-1003 | **Type:** Spatial | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** How many times does a coin roll around another identical coin to return to its starting position?
**A:** 2 times. (Coin rotation paradox).

**ID:** AAD-1004 | **Type:** Temporal | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** A twin paradox: Twin A stays on Earth. Twin B travels to a star 4 light-years away at 0.8c and returns. How much older is A than B?
**A:** Distance = 4 ly. Time for B (one way) = 4 / 0.8 = 5 years. Total trip for B = 10 years. $\gamma = 1/\sqrt{1-0.64} = 1/0.6 = 5/3$. Time for A = 10 * 5/3 = 16.67 years. A is 6.67 years older than B.

**ID:** AAD-1005 | **Type:** Causal | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** Does smoking cause lung cancer? How do we know, given we can't do a randomized controlled trial?
**A:** Yes. We know through epidemiological studies (Bradford Hill criteria), dose-response relationship, biological mechanism (carcinogens in smoke), and consistency across studies.

**ID:** AAD-1006 | **Type:** Logical | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** All cats are animals. Some animals are dogs. Therefore, some cats are dogs. Valid?
**A:** No. Fallacy of the undistributed middle.

**ID:** AAD-1007 | **Type:** Epistemic | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** What is the difference between knowledge and belief?
**A:** Knowledge is typically defined as Justified True Belief (JTB), though Gettier cases challenge this. Belief does not require truth or justification.

**ID:** AAD-1008 | **Type:** Counterfactual | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If the asteroid hadn't hit Earth 66 million years ago, would humans exist?
**A:** Unlikely. Mammals were small and nocturnal. The asteroid cleared ecological niches, allowing mammals to diversify and eventually evolve into primates and humans. Without it, dinosaurs might still dominate.

**ID:** AAD-1009 | **Type:** Analogical | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Code is to Programmer as Score is to ?
**A:** Composer.

**ID:** AAD-1010 | **Type:** Deductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** No A are B. All C are A. Therefore?
**A:** No C are B. (Celarent syllogism).

**ID:** AAD-1011 | **Type:** Inductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** A new drug cures 90% of patients in a trial of 100 people. Can we conclude it cures 90% of the general population?
**A:** No. The trial sample might not be representative (selection bias), and the confidence interval needs to be calculated.

**ID:** AAD-1012 | **Type:** Abductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** The universe is fine-tuned for life. What is the best explanation?
**A:** This is a philosophical debate. Explanations include: 1) Design (teleological), 2) Multiverse (selection bias), 3) Brute fact (it just is). Abductive reasoning here is highly subjective.

**ID:** AAD-1013 | **Type:** Spatial | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** A 3D object casts a circular shadow from the front and a square shadow from the side. What is the object?
**A:** A cylinder with its axis horizontal, or a cone, or a shape like a cylindrical wedge.

**ID:** AAD-1014 | **Type:** Temporal | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If you could travel back in time and kill your grandfather, what happens?
**A:** The grandfather paradox. If you kill him, you are never born, so you can't travel back to kill him. Resolutions include: Novikov self-consistency principle (you fail), or many-worlds interpretation (you create a branching timeline).

**ID:** AAD-1015 | **Type:** Causal | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** A rooster crows, and then the sun rises. Does the rooster cause the sun to rise?
**A:** No. Cum hoc ergo propter hoc / post hoc ergo propter hoc. The sun rises due to Earth's rotation.

**ID:** AAD-1016 | **Type:** Logical | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** "If this sentence is true, then God exists." Is this sentence logically valid?
**A:** This is Curry's paradox. In classical logic, if we assume the sentence is true, then the antecedent is true, so the consequent (God exists) must be true. This allows proving any statement, showing a flaw in naive truth theories.

**ID:** AAD-1017 | **Type:** Epistemic | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Can an AI truly "know" something, or does it just process data?
**A:** Philosophical debate. Searle's Chinese Room argues it's just syntax manipulation. Functionalists argue if it behaves as if it knows, it knows.

**ID:** AAD-1018 | **Type:** Counterfactual | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If water were not densest at 4°C, how would lakes freeze in winter?
**A:** They would freeze from the bottom up, killing aquatic life. The current property allows ice to float, insulating the water below.

**ID:** AAD-1019 | **Type:** Analogical | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** DNA is to Biology as ? is to Computer Science.
**A:** Source Code / Algorithm.

**ID:** AAD-1020 | **Type:** Deductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If P or Q. Not P. Therefore?
**A:** Q. (Disjunctive syllogism).

**ID:** AAD-1021 | **Type:** Inductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Every raven I've seen is black. Therefore, all ravens are black. What is the contrapositive observation that also confirms this?
**A:** Seeing a non-black object that is not a raven (e.g., a red apple). (Hempel's paradox).

**ID:** AAD-1022 | **Type:** Abductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Your car won't start, and the lights are dim. What's the most likely cause?
**A:** Dead battery. Best explanation for both symptoms.

**ID:** AAD-1023 | **Type:** Spatial | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** How many colors are needed to color a map on a torus so no adjacent regions share a color?
**A:** 7. (Heawood conjecture, proven for torus).

**ID:** AAD-1024 | **Type:** Temporal | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If you watch a clock for 12 hours, how many times do the hands overlap?
**A:** 11 times.

**ID:** AAD-1025 | **Type:** Causal | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** Does watching violent media cause violent behavior in children?
**A:** Correlated, but causation is debated. Confounding variables (family environment, genetics) make it hard to isolate. Longitudinal studies suggest a small causal effect, but it's not the primary cause.

**ID:** AAD-1026 | **Type:** Logical | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If A then B. If C then B. Therefore, if A then C. Valid?
**A:** No. Fallacy of the consequent.

**ID:** AAD-1027 | **Type:** Epistemic | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** What is the Münchhausen trilemma?
**A:** The argument that any attempt to prove a truth leads to either circular reasoning, infinite regress, or an unproven axiom.

**ID:** AAD-1028 | **Type:** Counterfactual | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If the speed of light were infinite, how would relativity change?
**A:** Special relativity would reduce to Galilean relativity. Simultaneity would be absolute. $E=mc^2$ would imply infinite energy for mass.

**ID:** AAD-1029 | **Type:** Analogical | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Teacher is to Student as Coach is to ?
**A:** Athlete / Player.

**ID:** AAD-1030 | **Type:** Deductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** All X are Y. Some Y are Z. Therefore, some X are Z. Valid?
**A:** No. Undistributed middle.

**ID:** AAD-1031 | **Type:** Inductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** A poll of 1000 people shows Candidate A has 52% support. What is the margin of error?
**A:** Approx $\pm 3\%$ at 95% confidence. ($1/\sqrt{n}$).

**ID:** AAD-1032 | **Type:** Abductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** The universe is expanding. What caused it?
**A:** The Big Bang. Best current cosmological model based on redshift, CMB, etc.

**ID:** AAD-1033 | **Type:** Spatial | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Can you draw a graph with 5 vertices where every vertex is connected to every other vertex without lines crossing?
**A:** No. $K_5$ is non-planar. (Kuratowski's theorem).

**ID:** AAD-1034 | **Type:** Temporal | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If you travel at the speed of light, how much time passes for you?
**A:** Zero. Time dilation is infinite. (Though massive objects can't reach $c$).

**ID:** AAD-1035 | **Type:** Causal | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** A study shows people who drink coffee live longer. Does coffee cause longer life?
**A:** Not necessarily. Confounding variables (socioeconomic status, diet, exercise) might be the real cause.

**ID:** AAD-1036 | **Type:** Logical | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** "This statement is unprovable." If the system is consistent, is the statement true or false?
**A:** True. (Gödel's first incompleteness theorem).

**ID:** AAD-1037 | **Type:** Epistemic | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** What is the difference between a priori and a posteriori knowledge?
**A:** A priori is independent of experience (math, logic). A posteriori depends on experience (empirical science).

**ID:** AAD-1038 | **Type:** Counterfactual | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If dinosaurs hadn't gone extinct, would mammals have evolved intelligence?
**A:** Probably not. Dinosaurs occupied the large ecological niches, keeping mammals small and nocturnal.

**ID:** AAD-1039 | **Type:** Analogical | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** Neuron is to Brain as Transistor is to ?
**A:** CPU / Microprocessor.

**ID:** AAD-1040 | **Type:** Deductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If P then Q. Not Q. Therefore?
**A:** Not P. (Modus tollens).

**ID:** AAD-1041 | **Type:** Inductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Every time I let go of a ball, it falls. Therefore, gravity exists. Is this deductively valid?
**A:** No, it's inductive. We infer the unobservable cause (gravity) from observable effects.

**ID:** AAD-1042 | **Type:** Abductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** You hear a siren and see an ambulance. What happened?
**A:** There is a medical emergency. Best explanation.

**ID:** AAD-1043 | **Type:** Spatial | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** What is the volume of a sphere with a cylindrical hole drilled through its center, given the length of the hole is $L$?
**A:** $\frac{\pi L^3}{6}$. (Napkin ring problem). It depends only on $L$, not the sphere's radius.

**ID:** AAD-1044 | **Type:** Temporal | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If a year on Mars is 687 Earth days, how many Mars years are in 10 Earth years?
**A:** $10 \times 365.25 / 687 \approx 5.31$ Mars years.

**ID:** AAD-1045 | **Type:** Causal | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** Does the presence of police reduce crime?
**A:** Generally yes, but the marginal effect decreases, and it can lead to over-policing in certain communities. Causation is established through natural experiments and econometric studies.

**ID:** AAD-1046 | **Type:** Logical | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If A then B. If B then C. Therefore, if A then C. Valid?
**A:** Yes. Hypothetical syllogism.

**ID:** AAD-1047 | **Type:** Epistemic | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** What is the Gettier problem?
**A:** Cases where a person has a Justified True Belief, but intuitively it's not knowledge because the justification is based on luck or a false premise.

**ID:** AAD-1048 | **Type:** Counterfactual | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If the Earth were twice as massive, how would gravity change?
**A:** Surface gravity would double (assuming same radius). $g = GM/R^2$.

**ID:** AAD-1049 | **Type:** Analogical | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Book is to Library as File is to ?
**A:** Directory / Folder.

**ID:** AAD-1050 | **Type:** Deductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** All A are B. No B are C. Therefore?
**A:** No A are C. (Cesare syllogism).

**ID:** AAD-1051 | **Type:** Inductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** A machine has worked perfectly for 1000 days. Will it work on day 1001?
**A:** Inductively, yes. But deductively, no guarantee. (Problem of induction).

**ID:** AAD-1052 | **Type:** Abductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** The cosmic microwave background is uniform in all directions. What does this imply?
**A:** The early universe was in thermal equilibrium, supporting the Big Bang theory and inflation.

**ID:** AAD-1053 | **Type:** Spatial | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** How many sides does a hexagon have?
**A:** 6.

**ID:** AAD-1054 | **Type:** Temporal | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If you could travel faster than light, could you send a message to the past?
**A:** Yes, in special relativity, FTL travel implies time travel and causality violations (tachyonic antitelephone).

**ID:** AAD-1055 | **Type:** Causal | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Does eating breakfast cause better school performance?
**A:** Correlated, but causation is mixed. It might be a proxy for overall socioeconomic status and parental involvement.

**ID:** AAD-1056 | **Type:** Logical | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** "All Cretans are liars," said a Cretan. Is he telling the truth?
**A:** Epimenides paradox. If he's telling the truth, then he's a liar, so he's lying. If he's lying, then not all Cretans are liars, which is consistent. It's not a strict paradox like the Liar, but a logical puzzle.

**ID:** AAD-1057 | **Type:** Epistemic | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** What is Occam's Razor?
**A:** The principle that the simplest explanation is usually the best one. (Plurality should not be posited without necessity).

**ID:** AAD-1058 | **Type:** Counterfactual | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If the Internet had never been invented, how would globalization differ?
**A:** Much slower. Communication would rely on phone, fax, mail. Global supply chains would be less integrated. Cultural exchange would be limited.

**ID:** AAD-1059 | **Type:** Analogical | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** Heart is to Body as Router is to ?
**A:** Network.

**ID:** AAD-1060 | **Type:** Deductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If P then Q. Q. Therefore P. Valid?
**A:** No. Affirming the consequent.

**ID:** AAD-1061 | **Type:** Inductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Every swan I've seen is white. Therefore, all swans are white. What would falsify this?
**A:** Seeing a single black swan. (Popper's falsificationism).

**ID:** AAD-1062 | **Type:** Abductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** The patient has a rash, fever, and joint pain. What's the diagnosis?
**A:** Could be lupus, rheumatoid arthritis, or an infection. Abductive reasoning requires more tests to narrow it down.

**ID:** AAD-1063 | **Type:** Spatial | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** What is the shortest path between two points on a sphere?
**A:** A great circle arc.

**ID:** AAD-1064 | **Type:** Temporal | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If a pendulum has a period of 2 seconds on Earth, what is its period on the Moon (gravity is 1/6th)?
**A:** $T = 2\pi\sqrt{L/g}$. If $g$ is 1/6th, $T$ increases by $\sqrt{6} \approx 2.45$. So $2 \times 2.45 = 4.9$ seconds.

**ID:** AAD-1065 | **Type:** Causal | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** Does carbon dioxide cause global warming?
**A:** Yes. The greenhouse effect is a well-established physical mechanism. CO2 absorbs IR radiation, trapping heat.

**ID:** AAD-1066 | **Type:** Logical | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** If A then B. Not A. Therefore not B. Valid?
**A:** No. Denying the antecedent.

**ID:** AAD-1067 | **Type:** Epistemic | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** What is the difference between deductive and inductive reasoning?
**A:** Deductive guarantees the conclusion if premises are true. Inductive provides probability, not certainty.

**ID:** AAD-1068 | **Type:** Counterfactual | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** If the Earth were closer to the Sun, would we be able to survive?
**A:** Depends on how much closer. A little closer, maybe (Venus is too hot). Much closer, the oceans would boil, and life as we know it would be impossible.

**ID:** AAD-1069 | **Type:** Analogical | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Eye is to Light as Ear is to ?
**A:** Sound.

**ID:** AAD-1070 | **Type:** Deductive | **Diff:** 9
**Q:** Some A are B. All B are C. Therefore?
**A:** Some A are C. (Datisi syllogism).

**ID:** AAD-1071 | **Type:** Inductive | **Diff:** 10
**Q:** A new AI model passes the Turing test. Does it mean it's conscious?
**A:** No. The Turing test measures behavioral imitation, not internal subjective experience. Passing it is inductive evidence of intelligence, but not deductive proof of consciousness.

## Benchmark Complete

You have reached the end of the official AAD™ Version 1.0 benchmark.

Thank you for using AAD™ (Across All Domains Test).

AAD™ was created as an independent benchmark to evaluate frontier artificial intelligence systems across a broad range of domains, including reasoning, mathematics, science, programming, engineering, creativity, long-context understanding, instruction following, and knowledge application.

This release represents the official Version 1.4 benchmark containing **1071 evaluation questions**.

If you discover typographical errors, duplicate questions, formatting issues, or incorrect expected answers, please report them through the project's GitHub repository. Community feedback helps improve future releases while preserving the integrity of previous benchmark versions.

Future versions of AAD™ may introduce new domains, improved question quality, expanded evaluation capabilities, and additional benchmark releases.
